§ 63-33-1703(1) and (2) and satisfy the examination requirements of § 63-33-1703(3).
63-33-1711. Requirements of an occupational therapist for dry needling.
In addition to the powers and duties granted to or imposed by this chapter, the
commissioner has the authority to establish minimum competency requirements that an
occupational therapist must demonstrate in order to practice dry needling of the upper
limb.

Section 93:
SECTION 84. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-1801. Part definitions.
- 190 - 012037
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Advertise" includes the issuing or causing to be distributed a card,
sign, or device to a person, or the causing, permitting, or allowing a sign or
marking on or in a building or structure, or in a newspaper or magazine, in a
directory, or on radio or television or by advertising by any other means designed
to secure public attention;
(2) "Appraisal activities":
(A) Means selecting, administering, scoring, and interpreting
instruments designed to assess an individual's aptitudes, achievements,
or interests, which are used to understand, measure, or facilitate the
individual's normal human growth and development, but does not include
the use of projective techniques in the assessment of personality, nor the
use of psychological or clinical tests designed to identify or classify
abnormal or pathological human behavior, nor the use of individually
administered intelligence tests; and
(B) Includes with regard to licensed professional counselors,
consistent with each counselor's formal education and training,
administering and utilizing appropriate assessment instruments that
measure or diagnose problems or dysfunctions within the context of
human growth and development as part of the counseling process or in
the development of a treatment plan;
(3) "Approved supervisor" means a licensed marital and family therapist,
psychologist, or psychiatrist who is either an American Association for Marriage
and Family Therapy-approved supervisor or a commissioner-approved marriage
and family supervisor;
(4) "Commissioner-approved marriage and family supervisor" means a
person who gives to the commissioner evidence of:
- 191 - 012037
(A) Five (5) years of full-time experience in marriage and family
therapy practice and supervision;
(B) Thirty-six (36) hours of supervision specifically in the skill of
providing marriage and family therapy supervision; and
(C) A recommendation for commissioner-approved supervisor
status from a supervisor who provided supervision for the supervision
referred to in subdivision (a)(4)(B);
(5) "Counseling" means assisting an individual, through the counseling
relationship, in a manner intended to facilitate normal human growth and
development, using a combination of mental health and human development
principles, methods, and techniques, to achieve mental, emotional, physical,
social, moral, educational, spiritual, or career development and adjustment
throughout the life span;
(6) "Licensed marital and family therapist" means a person to whom a
license has been issued pursuant to this part, which license is in force and not
suspended or revoked as of the particular time in question;
(7) "Licensed professional counselor" means a person licensed under
this part who is professionally trained in counseling and guidance services
designed to facilitate normal human growth and development through individual,
family, or group counseling, educational procedures, assessment, consultation,
and research and who assists individuals by the practice of counseling with their
personal, social, career, or educational development as they pass through life
stages;
(8) "Marital and family therapy" means the diagnosis and treatment of
cognitive, affective, and behavioral problems and dysfunctions within the context
of marital and family systems, and involves the professional application of
psychotherapeutic family systems theories and techniques in the delivery of
- 192 - 012037
services to individuals in the context of family systems theory and practice,
couples, and families;
(9) "Practice of counseling":
(A) Means rendering or offering to render to individuals, groups,
organizations, or the general public a service involving the application of
principles, techniques, methods, or procedures of the counseling
profession, including appraisal activities, counseling, consulting, and
referral activities; and
(B) Does not include permitting the treatment of a mental,
emotional, or adjustment disorder other than marital problems, parent-
child problems, child and adolescent antisocial behavior, adult antisocial
behavior, other specified family circumstances, other interpersonal
problems, phase of life problems, other life circumstance problems,
occupational problems, and uncomplicated bereavement, except as
provided in subdivision (10);
(10) "Practice of counseling as a mental health service provider":
(A) Means the application of mental health and human
development principles in order to:
(i) Facilitate human development and adjustment
throughout the life span;
(ii) Prevent, diagnose, and treat mental, emotional, or
behavioral disorders and associated disorders that interfere with
mental health;
(iii) Conduct assessments and diagnoses for the purpose
of establishing treatment goals and objectives within the
limitations prescribed in subdivision (2); and
- 193 - 012037
(iv) Plan, implement, and evaluate treatment plans using
counseling treatment interventions. As used in this subdivision
(10)(A)(iv), "counseling treatment interventions" means the
application of cognitive, affective, behavioral, and systemic
counseling strategies that include principles of development,
wellness, and pathology that reflect a pluralistic society; and
(B) Does not include the performance of an act that licensed
professional counselors designated as mental health service providers
are not educated and trained to perform or the designation of testing
reports as "psychological";
(11) "Practice of marital and family therapy" means the rendering of
professional marital and family therapy to individuals, couples, and family groups,
singly or in groups, whether such services are offered directly to the general
public or through organizations, either public or private, for a fee;
(12) "Recognized educational institution" means an educational
institution that is recognized by the commissioner and by a nationally or
regionally recognized educational or professional accrediting body;
(13) "Supervision" means the direct clinical review, for the purpose of
training or teaching, by an approved supervisor of a marriage and family
therapist's interaction with clients, where the purpose of supervision is to promote
the development of the practitioner's clinical skills; such supervision may include,
without being limited to, the review of case presentations, audiotapes,
videotapes, and direct observation; and
(14) "Use a title or description of" means to hold oneself out to the public
as having a particular status by means of stating such status on signs,
mailboxes, address plates, stationery, announcements, business cards, or other
instruments of professional identification.
- 194 - 012037
63-33-1802. Reciprocity for marital and family therapist applicants.
(a) The commissioner shall license without examination a marital and family
therapist applicant who is licensed to practice independently in another state if the
applicant's qualifications meet the licensure requirements under this part and part 1 of
this chapter.
(b) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses marital and family therapists.
63-33-1803. Required documentation from professional counselor applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
professional counselor must provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1)
(A) Has a conferred graduate degree in counseling or a closely
related field;
(B) Has obtained a total of sixty (60) graduate hours in counseling
or a closely related field; and
(C) Has completed a supervised field experience as either a
practicum or internship;
(2) Has had at least two (2) years of professional experience of a type
judged to be acceptable by the commissioner subsequent to being granted a
graduate degree and has not violated § 63-33-106 or § 63-33-1805;
(3) Has passed the examination offered by the National Board for
Certified Counselors (NBCC) or such other examination approved by the
commissioner;
(4) Has passed the jurisprudence exam in this state; and
(5) Has met additional criteria of the commissioner established by rule.
63-33-1804. Required documentation from marital and family therapist applicants.
- 195 - 012037
(a) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
marital and family therapist must provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Has met standards set by the commissioner no less stringent than the
American Association for Marriage and Family Therapy's standards for a clinical
member so long as such standards specify a minimum of a master's level
degree; and
(2) Has passed such examination as may be required by the
commissioner.
(b) Applicants shall bear the fee for testing in addition to the review fee and
application fee.
63-33-1805. Disciplinary grounds.
In addition to the disciplinary grounds listed in § 63-33-106(b), the commissioner
may also exercise the powers enumerated in § 63-33-106(a) for the following:
(1) Using fraud or deception in taking an examination required by this
part; or
(2) Violating the rules adopted by the commissioner, except that a
violation of A.11.b of the 2014 American Counseling Association Code of Ethics,
or any similar or successor provision, is not grounds upon which the
commissioner shall exercise the commissioner's powers to discipline a license;
however, a violation of A.11.b is a ground for the commissioner to exercise these
powers in cases involving an individual seeking or undergoing counseling where
the individual was in imminent danger of harming themselves or others.
63-33-1806. Exempted persons.
(a) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not apply to a person if the person is
preparing for the practice of marital and family therapy under qualified supervision in a
training institution or facility or supervisory arrangement recognized and approved by the
- 196 - 012037
commissioner as long as the person is designated by such titles as "marital therapy
intern," "family therapy trainee," or others clearly indicating such training status.
(b) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent:
(1) Qualified members of other professional groups as defined by the
commissioner by rule, including, but not limited to, licensed clinical social
workers, licensed psychologists, licensed psychological examiners, licensed
senior psychological examiners, certified psychological assistants, psychiatric
nurses, physicians, attorneys at law, or members of the clergy from doing or
advertising that they perform the work of a marital and family therapy nature
consistent with the accepted standards of their respective professions; and
(2) Alcohol and drug abuse counselors licensed under chapter 11, part 4
of this title or operating under qualified supervision while seeking such
certification from doing counseling consistent with the accepted standards of that
profession.
63-33-1807. Confidential relations and communications.
The confidential relations and communications between licensed marital and
family therapists, licensed professional counselors, or certified pastoral therapists and
clients are placed upon the same basis as those provided by law between attorney and
client. This part does not require such privileged communication to be disclosed.
However, this section and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent disclosures of confidential
communications in proceedings arising under title 37, chapter 1, part 4 concerning
mandatory child abuse reports.
63-33-1808. Prohibited conduct by unlicensed persons – Exemptions.
(a) Except as provided in § 63-33-1806, a person who is not licensed or certified
as a marital and family therapist under this part shall not:
(1) Advertise the performance of marital and family therapy or counseling
service by the person; or
- 197 - 012037
(2) Use a title or description, including, but not limited to, "licensed,"
"certified," "marriage," "marital," "therapist," "counselor," "advisor," or
"consultant," or any other name, style, or description denoting that the person is
a marital and family therapist or practices marital and family therapy.
(b) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section commits
a Class B misdemeanor.
(c) This part does not permit a person licensed or certified as a marital and
family therapist to engage in the practice of "licensed psychological examiner," "licensed
senior psychological examiner," "certified psychological assistant," "licensed
psychologist," or "licensed social worker," as defined in the laws of this state.
(d) This part, except subsection (a), does not apply to a person regulated by the
board of nursing.
(e) This part does not permit a person certified or licensed as a marital and
family therapist to perform psychological testing intended to measure or diagnose mental
illness. Consistent with each therapist's formal education and training, licensed marital
and family therapists may administer and utilize appropriate assessment instruments
that measure or diagnose cognitive, affective, and behavioral problems and dysfunctions
of individuals in the context of marital and family systems, couples, and families as part
of the therapy process or in the development of a treatment plan.
63-33-1809. Reciprocity for professional counselors.
(a)
(1) In accordance with § 63-33-104, the commissioner may issue a
license to a professional counselor applicant with a valid, unencumbered license
issued by another state, territory, or federal district of the United States at an
equivalent level of licensure under the following conditions:
(A) The applicant has a sixty-hour graduate degree in counseling
or a related field, meets the requirements of § 63-33-1803(2)-(5), and has
- 198 - 012037
actively practiced without supervision at the level of licensure for which
the applicant has applied for at least two (2) of the three (3) most recent
years; or
(B) The applicant has a conferred graduate degree consisting of a
minimum of fifty-two (52) hours in counseling or a related field from an
accredited program that were earned prior to 2016, has practiced as a
licensed professional counselor for a minimum of twenty-five (25) years,
and meets the requirements of § 63-33-1803(2)-(5).
(2) A professional counselor applicant at the highest level of licensure
must meet the requirements of § 63-33-1813, as well as the requirements of
either subdivision (a)(1)(A) or (a)(1)(B).
(b) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses, certifies, or registers professional counselors, if the board finds that such state
has substantially the same or higher licensure requirements than this state. The
agreement must provide that the board shall license a resident of another state who is
currently licensed, certified, or registered by that state, if the resident has met the same
or higher requirements as provided for in this part.
(c) If the commissioner has entered into a reciprocal agreement with another
state in accordance with § 63-33-104(b) on or before January 1, 2024, then the
commissioner must grant a license to a person who:
(1) Has a master's degree in counseling or education;
(2) Has a valid, unencumbered license in the state with which this state
has a reciprocal agreement;
(3) Has actively practiced for at least the preceding twenty-four (24)
months in the state with which this state has such reciprocal agreement; and
- 199 - 012037
(4) Has passed the examination offered by the National Board for
Certified Counselors (NBCC) or such other examination approved by the
commissioner.
63-33-1810. Unlawful use of titles – Exempt persons.
(a)
(1) Except as specifically provided elsewhere in this part, commencing
July 1, 2026, it is an offense for a person to engage in the following acts:
(A) Representing or advertising the person as, or using a title or
description such as, "licensed professional counselor" without being duly
licensed according to this part;
(B) Making use of a title, words, letters, or abbreviations, or any
combination thereof, that may reasonably be confused with licensure
provided by this part to denote a standard of professional or occupational
competence, without being duly licensed under this part; or
(C) Performing activities that may reasonably be construed to fall
within the defined scope of practice of persons licensed under this part
who are designated as mental health service providers as defined in § 63-
33-1813 without being duly licensed under this part.
(2) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section
commits a Class B misdemeanor.
(3) In addition to subdivisions (a)(1) and (2), the department of health
may institute appropriate proceedings, in law or equity, to enjoin a person from
engaging in an unlawful act enumerated in this section, such action or
proceeding to be brought in the circuit or chancery court of the county in which
the unlawful act occurs or in which the defendant resides.
(b) This part does not permit a person licensed or certified as a professional
counselor or designated as a mental health service provider under this part and part 1 of
- 200 - 012037
this chapter to engage in the practice of licensed psychological examiner, licensed
senior psychological examiner, certified psychological assistant, licensed psychologist,
licensed social worker, psychiatric nurse, law, or medicine.
(c) This part does not apply to a person if the person is preparing for the practice
of professional counseling or the practice permitted to a person designated as a mental
health service provider pursuant to this chapter under qualified supervision.
(d) This part does not:
(1) Limit the ministry, activities, or services of a rabbi, priest, minister of
the gospel, or others authorized by a regularly organized and functioning
religious body in performing the ordinary duties or functions of the clergy;
(2) Apply to or limit the activities or services of Christian Science
practitioners; or
(3) Limit a rabbi, priest, or minister who offers counseling services, even
if fees are charged, as long as they do not hold themselves out as certified or
licensed professional counselors.
63-33-1811. Exempted professionals.
(a) Except § 63-33-1810, this part does not apply to:
(1) Persons regulated by the board of nursing;
(2) Persons regulated by the state board of education; and
(3) Professional counselors employed in community or human services
agencies and working directly under the supervision of a licensed professional
counselor.
(b) This part does not prevent members of other professional groups, including,
without limitation, licensed social workers, psychologists, psychiatrists, and other
physicians, attorneys, or members of the clergy, from performing or advertising their
respective professions as long as such persons do not violate § 63-33-1810.
63-33-1812. Application of chapter 11 of this title.
- 201 - 012037
Notwithstanding this part to the contrary, a person licensed pursuant to this part
and chapter 11 of this title is subject to the limitations of chapter 11 of this title.
63-33-1813. Requirements of mental health service providers.
A professional counselor licensed under this part and designated as a mental
health service provider must have:
(1) Completed coursework specifically related to the diagnosis,
treatment, appraisal, and assessment of mental disorders; and
(2) Completed two (2) years of postgraduate supervised experience
required for licensure in a clinical setting that provides substantial opportunities to
diagnose, treat, appraise, and assess mental disorders.
63-33-1814. Temporary licenses.
(a)
(1) A temporary license may be issued by the commissioner for a
licensed professional counselor designated as a mental health service provider
applicant who has completed the academic coursework and training required for
the license sought and who has successfully passed the examination required by
the commissioner.
(2) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes an
applicant to perform the functions constituting the practice of counseling as a
mental health service provider, for which the applicant is seeking licensure under
qualified supervision.
(3) In order to receive a temporary license, an applicant must submit to
the division a completed application for a temporary license with the applicant's
completed application for the desired license and all appropriate fees.
(4) If an applicant is granted a temporary license, then the license must
remain valid for up to four (4) years and is eligible for extension at the discretion
of the commissioner.
- 202 - 012037
(5) The applicant shall notify the division and present supporting
documentation demonstrating the satisfactory completion of the required
postgraduate supervised experience in a clinical setting. The commissioner shall
then grant or deny the license application based on satisfactory completion of all
requirements for licensure.
(b)
(1) A temporary license may be issued by the commissioner to a marital
and family therapist applicant who has completed the academic coursework and
training required for the license sought. In order to retain the temporary license,
the applicant must take the written examination required by the commissioner the
first time it is scheduled following issuance of the temporary license. The
applicant shall successfully pass the exam within two (2) years following
issuance of the temporary license.
(2) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes the
applicant to engage in the practice of marital and family therapy under the
supervision of an approved supervisor.
(3) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant must submit to
the division the following:
(A) A completed application for a temporary license;
(B) Satisfactory evidence of an agreement with an approved
supervisor under whose supervision the applicant intends to practice; and
(C) All appropriate fees.
(4) A temporary license is nonrenewable and valid for a period of no
more than three (3) years. Within such three-year period, the applicant shall
submit to the division an application for the regular license and present
supporting documentation demonstrating the satisfactory completion of the
required amount of post-master's degree supervised experience in a clinical
- 203 - 012037
setting under an approved supervisor. The commissioner shall then grant or
deny the application for the regular license, based on satisfactory completion of
all requirements for licensure, including the oral examination. If the
commissioner approves or denies the application for the regular license or
revokes the temporary license for any reason, then the temporary license ceases
to be valid and must be returned to the division.
(5) The holder of a temporary license as a marital and family therapist
shall not represent the temporary licensee to be a licensed marital and family
therapist. The holder of the temporary license shall only represent the temporary
licensee to be a "marital therapy intern," a "family therapy trainee," or such other
title designation that clearly reflects trainee status and temporary licensure.

Section 94:
SECTION 85. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-1901. Part definitions.
As used in this part:
(1) "Advertise" includes:
(A) Business solicitations, with or without limiting qualifications, in
a card, sign, or device issued to a person, in a sign or marking in or on a
building or in a newspaper, magazine, directory, or other printed matter;
and
(B) Business solicitations communicated by individual, radio,
video or television broadcasting, or other means designed to secure
public attention;
(2) "Certified clinical pastoral therapist" means a person who has met the
qualifications for certified clinical pastoral therapist and holds a current,
unsuspended or unrevoked certificate that has been lawfully issued by the
commissioner;
- 204 - 012037
(3) "Clinical pastoral education" means a program of training, typically
occurring in general medical, psychiatric, or penal institutions, that is designed to
acquaint students of theology and practicing clergy with the clinical method of
learning, increase skills in the arts of pastoral care, and facilitate integration of a
professional pastoral identity;
(4) "Clinical pastoral therapy" means the diagnosis and treatment, from a
clinical pastoral perspective, of the psychodynamics, interpersonal dynamics,
and spiritual dynamics of persons experiencing emotional behavioral or relational
distress or dysfunction, and involves the integration and professional application
of resources and techniques from the religious community's traditions of pastoral
care and counsel along with recognized principles, methods, and procedures of
the contemporary psychotherapy community in the delivery of counseling and
psychotherapeutic services to individuals, couples, families, and groups;
(5) "Licensed clinical pastoral therapist" means a person who has met
the qualifications for a licensed clinical pastoral therapist and who holds a
current, unsuspended or unrevoked license that has been issued lawfully by the
commissioner;
(6) "Practice of clinical pastoral therapy" means the rendering of
professional clinical pastoral therapy to individuals, couples, families, or groups,
either offered directly to the general public by an individual operating
independently of an institution, organization, or agency, through mental health
clinics or agencies, whether public or private, or through hospitals, whether public
or private, for a fee, excluding volunteer hours;
(7) "Recognized educational institution" means an educational institution
that is accredited by a nationally or regionally recognized educational accrediting
body;
(8) "Supervision":
- 205 - 012037
(A) Means the direct clinical review, for the purpose of training or
teaching, by a commissioner-approved supervisor, of a clinical pastoral
therapist's interaction with clients and promoting the development of the
practitioner's clinical skills; and
(B) Includes the review of case presentations, audiotapes,
videotapes, and direct observation; and
(9) "Use the title" means to hold oneself out to the public as having a
particular status by means of stating such status on signs, mailboxes, address
plates, stationery, announcements, business cards, or other instruments of
professional identification.
63-33-1902. Prohibited conduct by unlicensed persons – Exemptions.
(a) Except as specifically provided in § 63-33-1904, a person who is not licensed
as a clinical pastoral therapist under this part shall not:
(1) Advertise that the performance of clinical pastoral therapy services is
by a licensed clinical pastoral therapist; or
(2) Use the title "licensed clinical pastoral therapist" to denote that the
person is a licensed clinical pastoral therapist.
(b) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section commits
a Class B misdemeanor.
(c) This section does not permit a person certified as a clinical pastoral therapist
to engage in the practice of licensed psychological examiner, licensed senior
psychological examiner, certified psychological assistant, licensed psychologist, or
licensed social worker, as defined in the laws of this state.
(d) This section does not apply to a person regulated by the board of nursing.
(e) This section does not permit a certified clinical pastoral therapist to prescribe
medications or to interpret psychological tests intended to measure or diagnose mental
illness.
- 206 - 012037
(f) Certified clinical pastoral therapists shall establish and maintain effective
working relationships with an interdisciplinary network of professionals, including at least
one (1) psychologically oriented physician, usually a psychiatrist, with an unlimited
license to practice the healing arts in this state, in order to make provision for referral for
the diagnosis and treatment of medical or mental conditions falling outside the scope of
clinical pastoral therapy.
63-33-1903. Documentation required from applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
clinical pastoral therapist shall provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Has met the educational standards set by the commissioner, which
must include:
(A) The completion of a course of studies consisting of a
minimum of sixty (60) graduate semester hours in a curriculum approved
by the commissioner, of which a minimum of nine (9) graduate semester
hours must relate specifically to the diagnosis and treatment of mental
disorders, and the awarding of a master's or doctoral degree from a
recognized educational institution; and
(B) The completion of a supervised clinical experience within the
academic degree program as either a practicum or internship that
includes experience in the assessment, diagnosis, and treatment of the
psychodynamics, interpersonal dynamics, and spiritual dynamics of
persons experiencing emotional, behavioral, relational, or spiritual
distress or dysfunction. The experience required under this subdivision
(1)(B) must be conducted under the supervision of a commissioner-
approved supervisor;
- 207 - 012037
(2) Has provided a minimum of one thousand four hundred (1,400) hours
of pastoral therapy with individuals, couples, families, or groups while receiving a
minimum of two hundred seventy (270) hours of supervision of such therapy
under commissioner-approved supervision; and
(3) Has passed examinations as approved by the commissioner.
63-33-1904. Religious, training, and professions exemptions.
(a) This part and part 18 of this chapter do not:
(1) Limit the ministry, activities, or services of a rabbi, priest, minister of
the gospel, or others authorized by a regularly organized and functioning
religious body in performing the ordinary duties or functions of the clergy;
(2) Apply to or limit the activities or services of Christian Science
practitioners; and
(3) Limit a rabbi, priest, or minister who offers counseling services, even
if fees are charged, as long as they do not hold themselves out as licensed
pastoral therapists or licensed pastoral counselors and do not purport to provide
the integration and professional application of resources and techniques from the
religious community's traditions of pastoral care and counsel along with
recognized principles, methods, and procedures of clinical psychotherapy.
(b) This part does not apply to a person if the person is preparing for the practice
of clinical pastoral therapy under qualified supervision in a training institution or facility or
supervisory arrangement recognized and approved by the commissioner as long as the
person is designated by such title as "pastoral therapy intern," "pastoral therapy trainee,"
or others clearly indicating such training status.
(c) This part does not prevent:
(1) Qualified members of other professional groups as defined by the
commissioner by rule, including, but not limited to, licensed clinical social
workers, licensed psychologists, licensed psychological examiners, licensed
- 208 - 012037
senior psychological examiners, certified psychological assistants, psychiatric
nurses, physicians, or attorneys at law, from performing or advertising that they
provide or offer counseling services consistent with the accepted standards of
their respective professions; and
(2) Alcohol and drug abuse counselors licensed under chapter 11, part 4
of this title or operating under qualified supervision while seeking such licensure
from doing counseling consistent with the accepted standards of such profession.
63-33-1905. Reciprocity – License by endorsement.
(a) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses, certifies, or registers clinical pastoral therapists, if the board finds that such
state has substantially the same or higher licensure requirements than this state. The
agreement must provide that the board may license without examination a resident of
another state who is currently licensed, certified, or registered by the state, if that
resident has met the same or higher requirements as provided in this part.
(b) The commissioner may license by endorsement a clinical pastoral therapist
applicant who is a fellow or diplomate of the American Association of Pastoral
Counselors if that person otherwise meets the requirements of this chapter.
(c) The commissioner may also license by endorsement a clinical pastoral
therapist applicant who is:
(1) Certified as a clinical member of the American Association of Pastoral
Counselors;
(2) Can document five (5) years of full-time practice in pastoral therapy
subsequent to AAPC certification; and
(3) Otherwise meets the requirements of this part.
63-33-1906. License for persons certified on or before June 3, 2003.
A person who was certified as a certified clinical pastoral therapist on or before
June 3, 2003, must be issued a license as a licensed clinical pastoral therapist when the
- 209 - 012037
person's certification is renewed or upon request of the person before the expiration of
the person's current certification.
63-33-1907. Temporary license.
(a) The commissioner may issue a temporary license to a clinical pastoral
therapist applicant who has completed the academic coursework and supervised clinical
experience for the license sought. In order to retain the temporary license, the applicant
must take the written examination required by the commissioner the first time it is
scheduled following issuance of the temporary license unless granted an extension by
the commissioner after submitting a written request to the division and making a showing
of good cause as determined by the commissioner. The applicant shall successfully
pass the exam within two (2) years following issuance of the temporary license unless
the applicant receives a good cause extension from the commissioner. An applicant
must only receive one (1) good cause extension from the commissioner.
(b) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes the
applicant to engage in the practice of clinical pastoral therapy under the supervision of a
commissioner-approved supervisor.
(c) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant must submit to the
division the following:
(1) A completed application for a temporary license;
(2) Satisfactory evidence of an agreement with a commissioner-approved
supervisor; and
(3) All required fees.
(d) A temporary license is nonrenewable and valid for a period of not more than
three (3) years. A temporary license may be extended beyond the three-year period at
the discretion of the commissioner if an applicant shows good cause for an extension as
determined by the commissioner. Only one (1) extension may be granted by the
commissioner for an applicant to extend the length of the applicant's temporary license.
- 210 - 012037
Within the period of temporary licensure, the applicant shall submit to the division an
application for the regular license and present supporting documentation demonstrating
the satisfactory completion of the required supervised clinical experience. The
commissioner shall then grant or deny the application for the regular license, based on
satisfactory completion of all requirements for licensure. If the commissioner approves
or denies the application for the regular license or revokes the temporary license for any
reason, then the temporary license ceases to be valid and must be returned to the
division.
(e) The holder of a temporary license as a clinical pastoral therapist shall not
represent the holder to be a licensed clinical pastoral therapist. The holder of a
temporary license as a clinical pastoral therapist shall only represent the holder to be a
"pastoral therapy intern," a "pastoral therapy trainee," or such other title designation that
clearly reflects trainee status and temporary licensure.
63-33-1908. Confidential relations and communications.
The confidential relations and communications between certified clinical pastoral
therapists and clients are placed upon the same basis as those provided by law between
attorney and client. This part does not require such privileged communication to be
disclosed. However, this section and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent disclosures of
confidential communications in proceedings arising under title 37, chapter 1, part 4,
concerning mandatory child abuse reports.

Section 95:
SECTION 86. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-2001. Part definitions.
As used in this part, "counseling or therapy services" means assisting an
individual, who is seeking or engaged in the counseling relationship in a private practice
setting, in a manner intended to facilitate normal human growth and development, using
a combination of mental health and human development principles, methods, and
- 211 - 012037
techniques, to achieve mental, emotional, physical, social, moral, educational, spiritual,
or career development and adjustment throughout the individual's life span.
63-33-2002. Client with goals, outcomes, or behaviors in conflict with sincerely
held principles of counselor or therapist – Refusal to provide counseling or therapy
services.
(a) A counselor or therapist providing counseling or therapy services is not
required to counsel or serve a client as to goals, outcomes, or behaviors that conflict
with the sincerely held principles of the counselor or therapist if the counselor or
therapist coordinates a referral of the client to another counselor or therapist who will
provide the counseling or therapy.
(b) The refusal to provide counseling or therapy services as described in
subsection (a) is not a basis for:
(1) A civil cause of action; or
(2) Criminal prosecution.
(c) Subsections (a) and (b) do not apply to a counselor or therapist when the
individual seeking or undergoing counseling is in imminent danger of harming
themselves or others.

Section 102:
SECTION 93. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 68, Chapter 1, Part 1, is amended by
adding the following as a new section:
68-1-150. Rules.
(a) When legislation is enacted by the general assembly that requires a board
administratively attached to the department to promulgate rules in a prescribed period of
time, the board retains the exclusive authority to promulgate the rules until sixty (60)
days before the effective date of the legislation.
(b) If the board has not promulgated emergency rules and scheduled the
rulemaking hearing on permanent rules at least sixty (60) days before the effective date
- 214 - 012037
of the legislation, the commissioner becomes the exclusive authority to promulgate the
rules as described in subsection (a). Upon the receipt of such authority, the
commissioner shall, in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5:
(1) Promulgate emergency rules, in accordance with § 4-5-208, within
the time required by the legislation; and
(2) Promulgate permanent rules within one hundred eighty (180) days of
the effective date of the emergency rules.
(c) Upon the completion of the requirements of subsection (b), the exclusive
authority to promulgate rules reverts to the board. The board may, at that time, amend
the permanent rules in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(d) The rules promulgated by the commissioner in accordance with subsection
(b) remain in full force and effect, the same as if promulgated by the board, unless and
until the rules are amended by the board.

SECTION 28. Tennessee Code Annotated, Section 63-1-120, is amended by deleting
the section and substituting the following:
(a)
(1) With respect to a person required to be licensed, permitted, certified,
or authorized by a board, council, committee, agency, or regulatory program
created pursuant to chapters 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12, 17, 19, 23, 29, and 33 of
this title and to title 68, chapter 140, attached to the division of health related
boards, such board, council, committee, agency, or regulatory program may:
(A) Deny an application for licensure, certification, permit, or
authorization;
(B) Permanently withhold issuance of licensure, certification,
permit, or authorization;
- 5 - 012037

(C) Suspend, limit, or restrict previously issued licensure,
certification, permit, or authorization; or
(D) Otherwise discipline a holder of a license, certificate, permit,
or authorization, if the applicant, licensee, or certificate or permit holder
has been disciplined by another state of the United States for any acts or
omissions that would constitute grounds for discipline of a person
licensed, certified, permitted, or authorized in this state.
(2) A certified copy of the initial order, final order, or other equivalent
document memorializing the disciplinary action from the disciplining state
constitutes prima facie evidence of a violation of this section and is sufficient
grounds upon which to deny, restrict, or condition the license, permit, or
certificate renewal or application, or to otherwise discipline a licensee licensed in
this state.
(b) In disciplinary actions against individuals holding a license, certificate, permit,
or authorization in this state at the time of a disciplinary action in another reporting state,
in the absence of justifying evidence to the contrary, there is a rebuttable presumption
that the sanction proposed in the proceeding is comparable to that in the reporting state;
however, such presumption does not exist for those who are applying for licensure,
certification, permit, or authorization in this state during or after the time the disciplinary
action in the other state is pending or has become final. If a board, council, committee,
agency, or regulatory program created pursuant to chapters 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12,
17, 19, 23, 29, and 33 of this title or title 68, chapter 140 denies, restricts, or conditions a
licensure, certification, permit, or authorization based on a disciplinary action in another
state, then the applicant, upon written request, filed within thirty (30) days of the date of
the action on the application, is entitled to a contested case hearing.

SECTION 45. Tennessee Code Annotated, Section 63-5-107(c)(1)(A), is amended by
deleting the subdivision and substituting:
(A)
(i) Each person licensed as a dentist or dental hygienist, or registered as
a dental assistant, is required to attend and complete during each two-year
licensure cycle, except for the initial licensure cycle and the first licensure
renewal cycle, the number of hours of board-approved continuing education
courses that are prescribed by the board, subject to a minimum of twenty-four
(24), and a maximum of sixty (60), clock hours. However, for the purposes of the
biennial continuing education requirement for dental hygienists, no more than fifty
percent (50%) of such continuing education requirement may be earned from
online or web-based courses. Sponsors of such courses shall submit a sufficient
description of course content to the board in order to obtain approval.
(ii) The board may approve all, part, or none of the course at its
discretion. Additional procedures for implementing this requirement may be
adopted by the board in its rules. The board may waive all or part of the
continuing education requirements in unusual situations in which an applicant for
renewal has demonstrated inability to attend such courses not attributable to fault
of the applicant. The board has discretion to require completion of continuing
education courses of a type and number of hours satisfactory to the board in
cases involving license renewal of dentists or dental hygienists who have not
actively practiced or have been retired from practice for more than two (2) years.
(iii) In addition to subdivisions (c)(1)(A)(i) and (ii), all applicants shall
provide proof of current CPR certification by an organization approved by the
board and maintain such certification unless such requirement is waived by the
board in its discretion; provided, that a dentist who obtains a waiver from the
- 10 - 012037

board for CPR requirements shall not practice dentistry unless a dentist, dental
hygienist, or dental assistant who is currently certified in CPR is present.

SECTION 51. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 11, Part 1, is amended
deleting the part and substituting:
63-11-101. Chapter definitions.
As used in this chapter:
(1) "Board" means the board of examiners in psychology, created by §
63-11-102;
(2) "Commissioner" means the commissioner of health;
(3) "Department" means the department of health; and
(4) "Division" means the division of health related boards in the
department of health, created by § 63-1-101.
63-11-102. Creation – Membership – Immunity.
(a) There is created a board of examiners in psychology to consist of nine (9)
members who are appointed by the governor under conditions set forth in this part.
(b)
(1) Two (2) members must be chosen from, and be members of the
faculty with the rank of assistant professor or above of, the accredited colleges
and universities in the state and be engaged in teaching, research, or
administration of psychology.
(2) Four (4) members must be licensed psychologists.
- 12 - 012037

(3) One (1) member must be a private citizen who is neither a licensed
psychologist nor a licensed psychological examiner or licensed senior
psychological examiner and who has no professional or commercial interest in
the practice of psychology.
(4) One (1) member must be a licensed applied behavioral analyst.
(5) One (1) member must be a licensed alcohol and drug counselor.
(c) The board shall perform such duties and exercise such powers as this
chapter prescribes and confers upon it.
(d) Members of the board are not liable to civil actions for any act performed in
good faith in the performance of their duties as set forth in this chapter.
63-11-103. Appointments – Vacancies.
(a) All appointments are for terms of five (5) years.
(b) Vacancies must be filled for any unexpired terms, and members shall serve
until their successors are appointed and have been qualified. Only practicing
psychologists must be appointed to succeed practicing psychologists, and only
academic psychologists must be appointed to succeed academic psychologists. Board
members are ineligible for reappointments for a period of five (5) years following
completion of their terms.
(c)
(1) Appointments to the board for the psychologist members may be
made from lists of qualified candidates to be furnished to the governor by
interested psychology groups, including, but not limited to, the Tennessee
Psychological Association. Each list must contain the names of academic
psychologists and practicing psychologists. All vacancies occurring in the board
may be filled by the governor for the unexpired term from the lists of qualified
candidates within thirty (30) days after the vacancy occurs. The governor shall
- 13 - 012037

consult with such interested groups to determine qualified persons to fill positions
on the board.
(2) In making appointments to the board, the governor shall strive to
ensure that at least one (1) person serving on the board is sixty (60) years of age
or older.
63-11-104. Oath of office – Records.
(a) Immediately and before entering upon the duties of the office, the members
of the board shall take the constitutional oath of office and file the same in the office of
the governor.
(b) The board shall have available for the governor adequate records of its
proceedings and of all licenses and certificates.
63-11-105. Organization – Administration.
(a) The board shall elect annually a chair and vice chair.
(b) Each member must receive all necessary expenses incident to conducting
the business of the board and, in addition thereto, be entitled to a per diem of one
hundred dollars ($100) for each day's service in conducting the business of the board.
All reimbursements for travel expenses must be in accordance with the comprehensive
travel regulations as promulgated by the department of finance and administration and
approved by the attorney general and reporter.
(c) The board shall hold at least one (1) regular meeting each year. Called
meetings may be held at the discretion of the chair or at the written request of two (2)
members of the board.
(d) The board shall adopt a seal, which must be affixed to all certificates issued
by the board.
(e) Six (6) members of the board at all times constitute a quorum. An action
taken by the board requires the majority of the quorum present.
- 14 - 012037

(f) The board is empowered to hire such assistance as is necessary to carry on
its activities, within the limits of funds available to the board, and is empowered to accept
grants from foundations or institutions to develop tests and carry out its functions.
(g) The board shall receive administrative support from the division.
(h) The board shall establish continuing educational requirements for all licenses
created in this chapter.
63-11-106. Powers and duties.
(a) The board has the following powers and duties in addition to the powers and
duties granted to or imposed upon it by this chapter:
(1) To prescribe rules for examination of candidates for a license created
by this chapter;
(2) To ascertain the qualifications and fitness of applicants for all licenses
created by this chapter;
(3) To issue licenses to applicants who successfully meet the
qualifications for licensure under this chapter and the board's rules;
(4) To receive complaints and review issues related to complaints and
disciplinary actions involving a person licensed under this chapter;
(5) To conduct investigations, as appropriate, into allegations against
licensees of the board;
(6) To issue private letter rulings in accordance with § 63-1-174;
(7) To make rules and establish fees as are necessary to carry out and
make effective this chapter; and
(8) To administer oaths, summon witnesses, and take testimony in all
matters relating to the board's duties.
(b) All rules promulgated by the board must comply with the Uniform
Administrative Procedures Act, compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
- 15 - 012037

(c) The board shall use the division-employed investigators, inspectors, and
agents, or use any other means necessary, to bring about and maintain the rigid
administration and enforcement of this chapter and all laws regulating the practice of a
profession created by this chapter.
(d) The board may maintain the existing separate accounts established for the
boards and committee that formerly licensed the professions now listed in this chapter;
provided, the division combines the revenue collected such that the division may use the
revenue of each account to offset expenditures across the accounts for this board.
Funds remaining in these accounts at the end of any fiscal year do not revert to the
general fund but must remain available for expenditure in accordance with law.
63-11-107. License – Application.
(a) Applicants for a license created by this chapter shall submit an application on
the form created by the board and any required fees to the division.
(b) In addition to the specific requirements for licensure in this chapter, the
application must include evidence that the applicant meets the following requirements:
(1) The applicant is of good moral character and conducts the applicant's
professional activities in accordance with the accepted professional and ethical
standards;
(2) The applicant has not had a professional credential refused, revoked,
suspended, or restricted and does not have a complaint, allegation, or
investigation pending in any regulatory jurisdiction in the United States or in
another country for unprofessional conduct, and has not committed an act that
would constitute grounds for discipline of a license under § 63-11-109; and
(3) The applicant is either a United States citizen or is lawfully present in
the United States in accordance with § 4-58-103(a)(1).
(c) The division and applicant shall comply with the criminal background
requirements of § 63-1-116.
- 16 - 012037

(d) Each applicant seeking licensure must pay all fees as set by the board,
including, but not limited to, nonrefundable application fees and examination fees.
(e) All licensees must comply with § 63-1-109.
(f) Portions of an application involving an applicant's health condition, including
mental health conditions and substance use disorders, and records involving an
applicant's health condition, are confidential, privileged, and not public records subject to
inspection by citizens of this state, as described in § 10-7-503.
(g)
(1) When the board receives a completed application for initial licensure,
or a completed application for licensure, from an applicant who is licensed in
another state or territory of the United States or in the District of Columbia, then
the board shall, within sixty (60) days from the date the board receives the
completed application:
(A) Render a decision on the application; or
(B) Inform the applicant of the need to appear before the board.
(2) As used in this subsection (g), "completed application" means an
application that satisfies all statutory and board rule requirements.
63-11-108. License renewal – Retirement.
(a) A license issued under this chapter is valid for twenty-four (24) months from
the date of issuance and is renewable biennially at the end of the birth month of the
licensee. The division, with the approval of the commissioner, shall establish a system
of license or certification renewals at alternative intervals that allow for the distribution of
the license or certification workload as uniformly as is practicable throughout the
calendar year. Licenses or certificates issued under the alternative method are valid for
twenty-four (24) months and expire on the last day of the last month of the license or
certification period.
- 17 - 012037

(b) In addition to any requirements of this chapter creating the license, a
licensee requesting renewal of a certificate must provide the following to the division in
advance of the expiration date of the license:
(1) A completed application on a form provided by the division and
payment of the fees set by the board; and
(2) A certified or sworn statement that the licensee:
(A) Has completed all the continuing education hours required for
the licensee, whether required by statute or rule, prior to the expiration
date of the license; and
(B) Has not had a professional credential revoked, suspended, or
restricted by a certification board, and does not have a complaint,
allegation, or investigation pending in this state or in any regulatory
jurisdiction for unethical or unprofessional conduct.
(c) If a licensee fails to pay the license renewal fee within sixty (60) days after it
becomes due, as provided in this section, the licensee must apply for a new license
rather than renew the existing license.
(d) A licensee who has lost the ability to renew pursuant to subsection (c) may
make application in writing to the board for the reinstatement of the license, and, upon
good cause shown, the board, in its discretion, may reinstate the license upon payment
of all past due renewal fees and upon further payment of a sum set by the board.
(e) Applicants and licensees shall notify the board of the following within thirty
(30) days of their occurrence:
(1) A change of name, address, or other vital information;
(2) The filing of a criminal charge or civil action against the applicant or
licensee;
- 18 - 012037

(3) The initiation of disciplinary charges, investigations, findings, or
sanctions by a healthcare organization, federal or state agency, or other
professional association against the applicant or licensee; and
(4) Any other change in information provided by the applicant or licensee
to the division.
(f) A person licensed or certified to practice by this chapter who has retired or
may retire on or after the effective date of this act from such practice in this state must
not be made to register as required by this chapter if the person files with this board an
affidavit on a form to be furnished by the board, which affidavit must state the date on
which the person retired from such practice and such other facts as tend to verify the
retirement as the board deems necessary. If the person thereafter reengages in such
practice in this state, then the person must apply for registration with the board as
provided by this chapter and meet other requirements as may be set by the board.
(g) For the purpose of effecting service of process upon a licensee, the board
may notify the licensee by certified mail, return receipt requested, at the address on file
with the division.
63-11-109. License denial, suspension, or revocation – Disciplinary grounds –
Hearing.
(a) The board has the power:
(1) To deny an application for a license to an applicant who applies for
the same through reciprocity or otherwise;
(2) To permanently or temporarily withhold issuance of a license;
(3) To issue a license contingent upon such circumstances or
requirements as the board may determine;
(4) To issue a conditional license that is limited or restricted for such time
and in such manner as the board may determine, including a limited license of
temporary duration for applicants out of practice for an extended period of time;
- 19 - 012037

(5) To issue discipline to an applicant or licensee, or on a previously
issued license, including, but not limited to, private censures and warnings, public
reprimands, limits, restrictions, conditions, or suspension periods, for such time
and in such manner as the board may deem proper in its discretion;
(6) To discipline a licensee who has been disciplined by another state of
the United States for any acts or omissions that would constitute grounds for
discipline if licensed in this state, following the procedure in § 63-1-120; or
(7) To revoke, or permanently revoke, a license.
(b) The grounds upon which the board may exercise the powers enumerated in
subsection (a) include, but are not limited to:
(1) Engaging in unprofessional, dishonorable, or unethical conduct;
(2) Making false statements or representations, being guilty of fraud or
deceit in obtaining admission to practice, or being guilty of fraud or deceit in the
course of professional practice;
(3) Violating or attempting to violate, directly or indirectly, or assisting in
or abetting the violation of, or conspiring to violate, a criminal statute of this state,
this chapter, a rule promulgated by the board, or a lawful order of the board
issued pursuant to rules;
(4) Engaging in gross professional liability, or a pattern of continued or
repeated professional liability, ignorance, negligence, or incompetence, in the
course of practice;
(5) Being habitually intoxicated or personally misusing drugs, or using
intoxicating liquors, narcotics, controlled substances, controlled substance
analogues, or other drugs or stimulants, in such manner as to adversely affect
the person's ability to safely practice in the profession;
(6) Willfully betraying a professional secret;
- 20 - 012037

(7) Advertising the professional practice with untrue or misleading
statements or causing the publication or circulation of fraudulent advertising
relative to any disease, human ailment, or condition;
(8) Willfully violating the rules that may be promulgated by the board to
regulate advertising by practitioners who are under the jurisdiction of the board;
(9) Being convicted of a felony, an offense under state or federal laws
relative to drugs or the professional practice, an offense involving moral
turpitude, or an offense for which the licensee or applicant is required to register
as a sexual offender or violent sexual offender pursuant to the Tennessee Sexual
Offender and Violent Sexual Offender Registration, Verification and Tracking Act
of 2004, compiled in title 40, chapter 39, part 2;
(10) Engaging in professional practice when mentally or physically
unable to safely do so;
(11) Making or signing in one's professional capacity a certificate that is
known to be false at the time one makes or signs the certificate;
(12) Offering, undertaking, or agreeing to cure or treat a disease, injury,
ailment, or infirmity by a secret means, method, device, or instrumentality;
(13) Giving, receiving, or aiding or abetting in the giving or receiving of
rebates, either directly or indirectly;
(14) Engaging in practice under a false or assumed name or the
impersonation of another practitioner of a like, similar, or different name;
(15) Practicing a level of psychology inappropriate or beyond the scope
of the particular license or licenses or certification held by the licensee or certified
person; and
(16) Engaging in any other action deemed to be grounds for disciplinary
action under rules promulgated by the board.
- 21 - 012037

(c) All proceedings for disciplinary action against a licensee under this chapter
must be conducted in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(d) An action taken under this section is subject to the applicable provisions of
the Fresh Start Act, compiled in chapter 1, part 1 of this title.
SECTION 52. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 11, Part 2, is amended by
deleting the part and substituting:
63-11-201. Levels of psychological practice.
(a) Five (5) levels of psychological practice are defined for the purposes of this
chapter. Such levels are to be known and referred to as:
(1) Psychological examiner;
(2) Senior psychological examiner;
(3) Psychologist;
(4) Certified psychological assistant; and
(5) Certified psychological testing technician.
(b) An individual who engages in the practice of psychology as a psychological
examiner, senior psychological examiner, or psychologist must possess a valid license
under this chapter.
(c) A person engaged in the practice of psychology as a certified psychological
assistant or certified psychological testing technician must possess a valid certificate to
practice under this chapter.
(d)
(1) This section does not prohibit a charitable clinic from employing or
contracting with a psychologist if the contractual relationship between the
psychologist and the charitable clinic is evidenced by a written contract, job
description, or documentation, containing language that does not restrict the
- 22 - 012037

psychologist from exercising independent professional judgment in diagnosing
and treating patients.
(2) As used in this subsection (d), "charitable clinic" means an entity that
meets the following standards:
(A) Has received a determination of exemption from the internal
revenue service under 26 U.S.C. § 501(c)(3) or is a distinct part of an
entity that has received such a determination of exemption;
(B) Has clinical facilities located in this state;
(C) Has a primary mission to provide health care or dental care
services to low-income, uninsured, or underserved individuals;
(D) Provides one (1) or more of the following services for free or
at a discounted rate:
(i) Medical care;
(ii) Dental care;
(iii) Mental health care; or
(iv) Prescription medications;
(E) Utilizes volunteer healthcare professionals and nonclinical
volunteers; and
(F) Is not required to be licensed under § 68-11-202(a)(1).
63-11-202. Practice of a psychological examiner.
(a) A person practices as a psychological examiner within the meaning of this
chapter when the person claims to be a psychological examiner or renders to individuals
or to the public health-related clinical activities or services involving the application of
recognized principles, methods, and procedures of the science and profession of
psychology, such as interviewing or administering and interpreting tests of mental
abilities, aptitudes, interests, and personality characteristics, for such purposes as
psychological evaluation or for educational or vocational selection, guidance, or
- 23 - 012037

placement. The psychological examiner shall practice the following health-related
clinical activities or services only under qualified supervision provided by a psychologist
or a senior psychological examiner:
(1) Overall personality appraisal or classification;
(2) Personality counseling;
(3) Psychotherapy;
(4) Behavior analysis; or
(5) Personality readjustment techniques.
(b) This section does not expand or restrict the scope of practice for a
psychological examiner.
(c) Those psychological examiners rendering health-related clinical activities or
services who have been duly licensed prior to July 1, 1991, who request to the board in
writing or via online application, are senior psychological examiners. Those duly
licensed psychological examiners rendering health-related clinical activities or services
licensed after July 1, 1991, qualify for senior psychological examiner licensure upon
completion of at least five (5) years of applied experience from the date their temporary
permit was first issued by the board and upon completion of two hundred (200) hours of
post-licensure continuing education units distributed by categories, according to the
November 1997 rules governing continuing education units. A person practices as a
senior psychological examiner within the meaning of this chapter when the person
claims to be a senior psychological examiner or renders to individuals or to the public for
remuneration a service involving the application of recognized principles, methods, and
procedures of the science and profession of psychology. A senior psychological
examiner, while possessing a different scope of practice than a psychologist, is
considered a health service provider and able to engage in the following designated
areas of health-related psychological practice without supervision:
- 24 - 012037

(1) Interviewing or administering and interpreting tests of mental abilities,
aptitudes, interests, and personality characteristics for such purposes as
psychological evaluation or for educational or vocational selection, guidance, or
placement;
(2) Overall personality appraisal or classification, psychological testing,
projective testing, and evaluations for disability or vocational purposes;
(3) Diagnosis of nervous and mental disorders;
(4) Personality counseling;
(5) Psychotherapy;
(6) Behavior analysis;
(7) Personality readjustment techniques; or
(8) Supervision of a psychological examiner.
63-11-203. Practice of a psychologist.
(a) As used in this part, "practice of psychology":
(1) Means, without regard to whether payment is received for services
rendered, the observation, description, evaluation, interpretation, and
modification of human behavior by the application of psychological principles,
methods, and procedures for the purpose of assessing, preventing, or eliminating
symptomatic, maladaptive, or undesired behavior and of enhancing interpersonal
relationships, work and life adjustment, personal effectiveness, behavioral health,
and mental health of individuals, families, groups, and the public; and
(2) Includes:
(A) Psychological testing and the evaluation or assessment of
personal characteristics, such as intelligence, personality, abilities,
interests, aptitudes, and neuropsychological functioning;
(B) Counseling, psychoanalysis, psychotherapy, hypnosis,
biofeedback, and behavior analysis and therapy;
- 25 - 012037

(C) Psychological diagnosis and treatment of mental, emotional,
and nervous disorders or disabilities; alcoholism and substance abuse;
disorders of habit or conduct; and psychological aspects of physical
illness, accident, injury, or disability;
(D) Case management and utilization review of psychological
services;
(E) Psychoeducational evaluation, therapy, remediation, and
consultation;
(F) Forensic evaluation; provided, that a person licensed under
this chapter performing forensic evaluation is considered to be acting
within their lawful scope of practice and the practice of forensic evaluation
is not exclusive to individuals licensed under this chapter;
(G) Parent coordination; provided, that a person licensed under
this chapter performing parent coordination is considered to be acting
within their lawful scope of practice and the practice of parent
coordination is not exclusive to individuals licensed under this chapter;
and
(H) Telepsychology, which means the practice of psychology via
electronic communications technology by a person licensed under this
chapter.
(b) A person represents to be a psychologist if that person uses a title or
description of services incorporating the words "psychology," "psychological," or
"psychologist," if the person possesses expert qualification in any area of psychology or
if that person offers to the public or renders to individuals or to groups of individuals
services pursuant to the practice of psychology.
63-11-204. Psychotherapy limitations – Conduct outside psychological practice
prohibited.
- 26 - 012037

(a) Sections 63-11-201 — 63-11-203 do not permit the use of those forms of
psychotherapy that involve the administration or prescription of drugs or electroshock or
in any way infringe upon the practice of medicine as defined in the laws of this state.
(b) A psychologist, psychological examiner, senior psychological examiner,
certified psychological assistant, or certified psychological testing technician who
engages in psychotherapy shall establish and maintain effective intercommunication with
a psychologically oriented physician, usually a psychiatrist, to make provision for the
diagnosis and treatment of medical problems by a physician with an unlimited license to
practice the healing arts in this state.
(c) A psychologist, psychological examiner, senior psychological examiner,
certified psychological assistant, or certified psychological testing technician shall not
attempt to diagnose, prescribe for, treat, or advise a client with reference to problems or
complaints falling outside the boundaries of psychological practice.
(d) Sections 63-11-203 and 63-11-208(c) and (d) are subject to the limitations of
this section.
63-11-205. Use of titles.
(a)
(1) Individuals and organizations shall not present themselves, or be
presented, to the public by a title incorporating the name "psychological,"
"psychologist," or "psychology" other than those licensed as psychologists,
psychological examiners, senior psychological examiners, certified psychological
assistants, or certified psychological testing technicians.
(2) A psychological scientist employed by a recognized research
laboratory, college, or university may use the academic or research title
conferred upon the psychological scientist by the administration of the laboratory,
college, or university.
- 27 - 012037

(3) Persons licensed by the state board of education in areas of school
psychology, school psychologist, or school psychological services worker and
employed as such in the department of education or in a public or nonpublic
elementary or secondary school are not required to be licensed under this part
while performing in the course of their employment. This chapter does not apply
to persons licensed by the state board of education in areas of school
psychology, school psychologist, or school psychological services worker who
are employed as such in the department of education or in a public or nonpublic
elementary or secondary school while performing in the course of their
employment.
(b) This section does not permit such persons to offer their services to any other
persons or organizations as consultants or to accept remuneration for psychological
services other than that of their institutional salaries unless they have been licensed or
certified under this chapter.
(c) Visiting lecturers from recognized laboratories, colleges, or universities are
exempt from this section and may utilize their academic or research title when
presenting lectures to similar institutions or organizations.
(d) Students of psychology, psychological interns, and other persons preparing
for the profession of psychological examiner, senior psychological examiner, certified
psychological assistant, certified psychological testing technician, or psychologist under
qualified supervision in recognized training institutions or facilities may be designated by
such titles as "psychological intern," "psychological trainee," or others clearly indicating
such training status.
(e) Psychologists with competency in areas other than the provision of health
services retain the right to use the title of "licensed psychologist" with competence in
areas other than health services and to practice within their area of competency.
63-11-206. Unauthorized practice – Exemptions – Temporary licenses.
- 28 - 012037

(a) A person who engages in the practice of psychology and does not then
possess in full force and virtue a valid license to practice as a psychological examiner,
psychologist, or senior psychological examiner, or a valid certificate to practice as a
psychological assistant or psychological testing technician, under this chapter commits a
Class B misdemeanor.
(b) This chapter does not prevent members of other recognized professions who
are licensed, certified, or regulated under the laws of this state from rendering services
consistent with their professional training and code of ethics as long as they do not
represent themselves to be psychologists, psychological examiners, senior
psychological examiners, certified psychological assistants, or certified psychological
testing technicians. Duly recognized members of the clergy are not restricted from
functioning in their ministerial capacity as long as they do not represent themselves to be
psychologists, psychological examiners, senior psychological examiners, certified
psychological assistants, or certified psychological testing technicians.
(c)
(1) Students of psychology, psychological interns, and other persons
preparing for the profession of psychological examiner, psychologist, senior
psychological examiner, certified psychological assistant, or certified
psychological testing technician may perform as a part of their training the
functions in §§ 63-11-202 and 63-11-203, but only under qualified supervision.
(2) A person practices as a certified psychological assistant within the
meaning of this chapter when the person claims to be a certified psychological
assistant or renders to individuals or to the public for remuneration a service
involving the application of recognized principles, methods, and procedures of
the science and profession of psychology and only under the direct employment
and supervision of either the psychologist or senior psychological examiner
employing the certified psychological assistant or the employing community
- 29 - 012037

mental health center or state governmental agency. All work performed by a
certified psychological assistant must be supervised by a psychologist or senior
psychological examiner as determined by the board.
(3) A person practices as a certified psychological testing technician
within the meaning of this chapter when the person claims to be a certified
psychological testing technician or renders to individuals or the public for
remuneration a service involving the application of recognized principles,
methods, and procedures of the science and profession of psychology and only
under the supervision of either the psychologist or senior psychological examiner
employing the certified psychological testing technician or the employing
community mental health center or state governmental agency. All work
performed by a certified psychological testing technician must be supervised by a
psychologist or senior psychological examiner as determined by the board.
(d) Use of psychological techniques by governmental institutions and by
business and industrial organizations for employment placement, evaluation, promotion,
or job adjustment of their own officers or employees or by employment agencies for the
evaluation of their own clients prior to recommendation for employment is also
specifically allowed; however, an industrial or business firm or corporation shall not sell
or offer to the public or to other firms or corporations for remuneration psychological
services as specified in §§ 63-11-202 and 63-11-203, unless the services are performed
or supervised by individuals duly and appropriately licensed under this chapter.
(e)
(1)
(A)
(i) The board may issue a temporary license to an
applicant who has successfully completed the academic course
- 30 - 012037

work and training for the license sought, and who has not yet
taken the required written examinations.
(ii) A temporary license is valid for a period not to exceed
one (1) year. The board may extend the expiration date of a
temporary license following a petition from the licensee and
finding that extraordinary circumstances exist that necessitate a
delay in taking a required written examination prior to the
expiration of the initial temporary license period.
(iii) A temporary license is revoked thirty (30) days after
the date a temporary licensee receives notice of the licensee's
second failure of the examination for professional practice in
psychology (EPPP) or jurisprudence examination. During the
thirty-day period prior to revocation of the temporary license, the
licensee and the licensee's supervisor shall ensure the notification
and transfer of care for the temporary licensee's clients.
(B) The temporary license allows the applicant to perform the
functions specified in §§ 63-11-202 and 63-11-203, for which the
applicant is seeking licensure under qualified supervision.
(C) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant must
submit a completed application for a temporary license with the
applicant's completed application for the desired license and all
appropriate fees to the board.
(2)
(A)
(i) A temporary license may be issued by the board for an
applicant who has a current license from another state or territory.
The temporary license allows the applicant to perform under
- 31 - 012037

qualified supervision the functions specified in §§ 63-11-202 and
63-11-203.
(ii) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant
must submit a completed application for a temporary license with
the applicant's completed application for the desired license and
all appropriate fees to the board.
(iii) Applications for temporary licenses for applicants
currently licensed in another state or territory must be reviewed
and approved or denied by a current member of the board
designated by the board to perform this function.
(iv) If an applicant is issued a temporary license, then the
license remains valid until the board grants or denies the license
application.
(v) However, a person must not be issued more than one
(1) temporary license, and a temporary license must not be valid
for a period of more than one (1) year.
(B) Such a temporary license may be issued to allow an applicant
