(b) In addition to the specific requirements for licensure of each part of this
chapter, the application must include evidence that the applicant meets the following
requirements:
(1) The applicant has attained the age of majority;
(2) The applicant is of good moral character and conducts the applicant's
professional activities in accordance with accepted professional and ethical
standards;
(3) The applicant has not had a professional credential refused, revoked,
suspended, or restricted and does not have a complaint, allegation, or
investigation pending in any regulatory jurisdiction in the United States or in
another country for unprofessional conduct, and has not committed an act that
would constitute grounds for discipline of a license under § 63-33-106; and
(4) The applicant is either a citizen of the United States or is lawfully
present in the United States in accordance with § 4-58-103(a)(1).
(c) The division and applicant shall comply with the criminal background check
requirements of § 63-1-116.
(d) All licensees shall comply with the requirements of § 63-1-109.
- 82 - 012037

(e) Portions of an application involving an applicant's health condition, including
mental health conditions and substance use disorders, and records involving an
applicant's health condition, are confidential, privileged, and not public records subject to
inspection by citizens of this state, as described in § 10-7-503.
(f)
(1) When the division receives a completed application for initial
licensure from an applicant, the division shall, within sixty (60) days from the date
the division receives the completed application:
(A) Render a decision on the application; or
(B) Inform the applicant of the need to appear before the
commissioner or the commissioner's designee.
(2) As used in this subsection (f), "completed application" means an
application that satisfies all statutory and board rule requirements.
63-33-104. Reciprocity.
(a) The commissioner may, at the commissioner's discretion, grant a license
created by this chapter to a person residing or employed in this state who is certified or
licensed by a similar entity in another state whose standards, as determined by the
commissioner, are not less stringent than the standards required by the part creating the
license.
(b) The commissioner may enter into a reciprocal agreement with another state
or jurisdiction that certifies or licenses persons engaged in the practice of a profession
licensed under this chapter if the commissioner determines that the other state has
substantially similar or more stringent certification or licensure requirements than this
state.
63-33-105. License renewal.
- 83 - 012037

(a) A license issued under this chapter is valid for twenty-four (24) months from
the date of issuance and is renewable biennially at the end of the birth month of the
licensee.
(b) In addition to any requirements of this chapter creating the license, a
licensee requesting renewal of a certificate shall provide the following to the division in
advance of the expiration date of the license:
(1) A completed application on a form provided by the division and
payment of the fees set by the commissioner; and
(2) A certified or sworn statement that the licensee:
(A) Has completed all the continuing education hours required for
the licensee, whether required by statute or by rule, prior to the expiration
date of the license; and
(B) Has not had a professional credential revoked, suspended, or
restricted by a certification board, and does not have a complaint,
allegation, or investigation pending in this state or in any regulatory
jurisdiction for unethical or unprofessional conduct.
(c) If a licensee fails to submit an application for license renewal, to pay any fee
required by the commissioner, or to submit a certified or sworn statement as set forth in
subdivision (b)(2) prior to the expiration date of the license, then the license is
automatically revoked by the commissioner without further notice or hearing, unless
renewal is completed and all fees are paid prior to the expiration of sixty (60) days from
the date of the expiration of the license.
(d) A person whose license is automatically revoked under this section may
apply in writing to the division for reinstatement of the license. Upon the showing of
good cause by the person and submitting documentation that all continuing education
requirements have been satisfied, the commissioner may reinstate the license upon the
payment of all fees set by the commissioner.
- 84 - 012037

(e) Applicants and licensees must notify the division of the following within thirty
(30) days of their occurrence:
(1) A change of name, address, or other vital information;
(2) The filing of any criminal charge or civil action against the applicant or
licensee;
(3) The initiation of any disciplinary charges, investigations, findings, or
sanctions by a healthcare organization, federal or state agency, or other
professional association against the applicant or licensee; and
(4) Any other change in information provided by the applicant or licensee
to the division.
(f) For the purpose of effecting service of process upon a licensee, the
commissioner or the division may notify the licensee by certified mail, return receipt
requested, at the address on file with the division.
(g) A person licensed or certified to practice by this chapter who has retired or
may retire from such practice on or after the effective date of this act is not required to
register as is required by this chapter if the person files with the division an affidavit on a
form to be furnished by the division, stating the date on which the person retired from
such practice and such other facts as tend to verify the retirement as the division deems
necessary. If the person thereafter reengages in such practice in this state, then the
person shall apply for licensure with the division as provided by this chapter and meet
other requirements as may be set by the commissioner.
63-33-106. License denial, suspension, or revocation – Grounds – Examinations –
Hearings.
(a) The commissioner has the power to:
(1) Deny an application for a license to any applicant who applies for the
same through reciprocity or otherwise;
(2) Permanently or temporarily withhold issuance of a license;
- 85 - 012037

(3) Issue a license contingent upon such circumstances or requirements
as the commissioner may determine;
(4) Issue a conditional license that is limited or restricted for such time
and in such manner as the commissioner may determine, including a limited
license of temporary duration for applicants out of practice for an extended period
of time;
(5) Issue discipline to an applicant or licensee, or on a previously issued
license, including, but not limited to, any combination of, private censures and
warnings, public reprimands, limits, restrictions, conditions, probation periods,
suspension periods, require participation in a peer assistance program, and issue
civil penalties for such time and in such manner as the commissioner may deem
proper in the commissioner's discretion;
(6) Discipline a licensee who has been disciplined by another state of the
United States for any acts or omissions that would constitute grounds for
discipline licensed in this state, following the procedure in § 63-1-120; or
(7) Revoke, or permanently revoke, a license.
(b) The grounds upon which the commissioner may exercise the powers
enumerated in subsection (a) include, but are not limited to:
(1) Engaging in unprofessional, dishonorable, or unethical conduct;
(2) Obtaining or attempting to obtain a license by making a false or
misleading statement, failing to make a required statement, or engaging in fraud
or deceit in any communication to the department;
(3) Violating or attempting to violate, directly or indirectly, or assisting in
or abetting the violation of, or conspiring to violate, a criminal statute of this state,
this part, a rule promulgated by the commissioner, or a lawful order of the
commissioner issued pursuant to rules;
- 86 - 012037

(4) Engaging in gross professional liability, or a pattern of continued or
repeated professional liability, ignorance, negligence, or incompetence, in
professional work;
(5) Being habitually intoxicated or personally misusing drugs, or using
intoxicating liquors, narcotics, controlled substances, controlled substance
analogues, or other drugs or stimulants, in such manner as to adversely affect
the person's ability to safely practice in the person's profession;
(6) Being convicted of a felony, any offense under state or federal laws
relative to drugs or the professional practice, an offense involving moral
turpitude, or any offense for which the licensee or applicant is required to register
as a sexual offender or violent sexual offender pursuant to the Tennessee Sexual
Offender and Violent Sexual Offender Registration, Verification and Tracking Act
of 2004, compiled in title 40, chapter 39, part 2;
(7) Engaging in professional practice when mentally or physically unable
to do so safely; and
(8) Engaging in any other action deemed to be grounds for disciplinary
action under rules promulgated or enforced by the commissioner.
(c) All proceedings for disciplinary action against a licensee under this chapter
must be conducted in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(d) Assessment and collection of costs must follow the requirements and
procedure contained in § 63-1-144.
(e) In enforcing this section, the commissioner shall, upon probable cause, have
authority to compel an applicant or licensee to submit to a mental or physical
examination, or both, by a designated committee of at least three (3) practicing
physicians, including a psychiatrist where a question of mental condition is involved.
The applicant or licensee may have an independent medical practitioner present during
- 87 - 012037

such examination, and the applicant may have an independent physical or mental
examination, which examination report must be filed with the commissioner for
consideration. The committee shall submit a report of its findings to the commissioner,
who must then hold a hearing governed by the Unform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(f) Notwithstanding § 63-1-122, for purposes of an action before the
commissioner for a license created and regulated under this chapter, in which the
standard of care is at issue, qualified expert testimony on the standard of care is
required. The standard of care for such actions is a statewide standard of minimal
competency and practice. The provisions of title 29, chapter 26, and specifically § 29-
26-115(a), concerning the locality rule, do not apply to disciplinary actions involving
licenses created under this chapter. However, expert testimony is not required to prove
a violation of unprofessional, dishonorable, or unethical conduct.
(g) A person whose license or certificate has been revoked by the commissioner
is not eligible to apply for reinstatement earlier than one (1) year from the date of
revocation.
63-33-107. Unlicensed practice.
(a) A person who engages in the practice of a profession licensed by the
commissioner without a current, valid license, and a person who violates this chapter,
commits a Class B misdemeanor. Each such engagement in unlicensed practice
constitutes a separate offense.
(b) The commissioner may assess civil penalties against a person engaged in
the practice of a profession licensed by the commissioner without a current, valid license
for each separate offense. The commissioner may also refer the case to law
enforcement.
(c) The commissioner may petition any circuit or chancery court having
jurisdiction of a person within this state who is practicing without a license, to whom a
- 88 - 012037

license has been denied, or whose license has been suspended or revoked, to enjoin
such person from continuing to practice the healing arts, or any branch thereof, within
this state. Jurisdiction is conferred upon the circuit and chancery courts of this state to
hear and determine all such causes as equity causes and exercise full and complete
jurisdiction in such injunctive proceedings.
(d) This section does not confer criminal jurisdiction upon a court not now
possessing such criminal jurisdiction, nor does any such court, as an incident to the
injunctive proceedings authorized in this section, have the power to assess the criminal
penalties set out in this chapter.
63-33-108. Delegation of powers.
(a) The commissioner may delegate any of the powers granted to the
commissioner in this chapter to any employee of the department. The commissioner
may also appoint consultant members of any health-licensed profession to work for a per
diem or hourly rate to review and evaluate licensure applications, disciplinary cases,
licensee inquiries, serve on state or national advisory boards or compact commissions,
and otherwise assist division staff as necessary to carry out this chapter.
(b) When appointing consultants pursuant to this section, the commissioner shall
consider recommendations made by interested professional associations related to the
licensure type at issue for the consultant's review.
63-33-109. Fees.
(a) By rule, the commissioner shall establish fees for all the license types
created under this chapter. These fees include, but are not limited to:
(1) Initial licensure application fee;
(2) Examination fee;
(3) Biennial licensure renewal fee;
(4) Late renewal fee;
(5) Licensure reinstatement fee;
- 89 - 012037

(6) Duplicate decorative license fee; and
(7) Reciprocal licensure fee.
(b) The commissioner shall ensure that the fees collected by the division for the
agency of commissioner issued licenses are sufficient in an amount to pay all the costs
associated with the administration, monitoring, and enforcement for all the licenses
created under this chapter.
63-33-110. Emergency rules.
To effectuate this chapter, the commissioner may promulgate emergency rules
pursuant to § 4-5-208(a)(5).
63-33-111. Validity of prior licenses, certificates, and registrations.
All licenses, certificates, and registrations regulated under chapters 3, 13, 16, 18,
22, 24, 25, 27, and 31, and valid as of June 30, 2026, must be transferred to the agency
of commissioner issued licenses and remain in effect on their current renewal cycles
under the authority of the commissioner pending the promulgation of any new rules on
the issuance and renewal of such licenses, certificates, and registrations, as necessary.
63-33-112. Transfer of rules and regulatory authority to the commissioner.
(a) As of July 1, 2026, the secretary of state shall cause the following rules to be
transferred to Tenn. Comp. R. & Reg. 1200-10:
(1) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0150-01;
(2) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0470-01;
(3) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0870-01 and 0870-02;
(4) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1330-01;
(5) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0880-14;
(6) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0880-12;
(7) All rules promulgated by the [former] professional art therapist
advisory committee of the board of examiners in psychology [repealed];
- 90 - 012037

(8) All rules promulgated by the [former] professional music therapy
advisory committee of the board of examiners in psychology [repealed];
(9) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1020-01 and 1020-02;
(10) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1155-01, 1155-02, 1155-03, and 1155-04;
(11) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1150-01 and 1150-02; and
(12) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0450-01, 0450-02, and 0450-03.
(b) The rules listed in subsection (a) must remain in effect pending the
promulgation of any new rules on the same subject in accordance with the Uniform
Administrative Procedures Act, compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(c) Effective July 1, 2026, the commissioner has the authority to regulate the
professions affected by the rules listed in subsection (a), including through use of those
rules, until new rules on the same subject are promulgated.
SECTION 70. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-201. Part definitions.
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Compensation" means the payment, loan, advance, donation,
contribution, deposit, or gift of money or anything of value;
(2) "Massage," "bodywork," and "somatic" mean the manipulation of the
soft tissues of the body with the intention of positively affecting the health and
well-being of the client;
(3) "Massage establishment" means a place of business held out to the
public wherein massage is practiced; and
(4) "Massage therapist" means a person who practices massage for
compensation and is licensed by the commissioner.
63-33-202. Practice of massage – Practice of reflexology.
- 91 - 012037

(a) Persons or massage establishments engaged in massage for compensation
must be licensed by the commissioner.
(b) It is unlawful to use the word "massage," or any other term that implies
massage technique or method, when advertising a service by a person who is not
licensed under this part or another chapter of state law.
(c) The practice of reflexology is not subject to the licensure requirements of this
chapter. As used in this subsection (c), "reflexology" means the application of specific
pressures to reflex points in the hands and feet only.
63-33-203. Documentation required from applicants.
(a)
(1) Except as provided in subdivision (a)(2) and in addition to the
requirements of § 63-33-103, each applicant for licensure as a massage therapist
shall provide documentation in the form required by the commissioner that the
applicant:
(A) Successfully completed the curriculum or curricula of one (1)
or more postsecondary academic institutions for massage, bodywork, or
somatic therapy as defined by board rules, totaling six hundred fifty (650)
hours or more, such institutions being approved by the commissioner
pursuant to § 63-33-209, and either authorized by the Tennessee higher
education commission, or its equivalent in other states, or approved, or
under the governance of, the board of regents; and
(B) Received a passing score on a competency examination
approved by the board.
(2)
(A) A person who has completed a program of study as required
by subdivision (a)(1)(A) in a postsecondary academic institution located in
this state and received a diploma or certificate prior to September 1,
- 92 - 012037

2005, must be issued a license without completing the examination
requirement in subdivision (a)(1)(B).
(B) A person who meets the requirements of subdivision (a)(2)(A)
has until January 1, 2006, to apply for such a license.
(C) Persons licensed under this subdivision (a)(2) are not
considered to have national certification and not hold themselves out to
be nationally certified.
(b) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, each applicant for licensure
as a massage establishment shall provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that each person engaged in massage at the massage establishment has
provided the documentation required in subsection (a) and has been licensed as a
massage therapist by the commissioner.
(c) Notwithstanding this part, an establishment license is not required for the
office of a physician licensed under chapter 4, 6, or 9 of this title if a massage for
compensation is provided within that office by a licensed massage therapist.
63-33-204. Inspections.
In order to effectuate this part, the commissioner may conduct an investigation of
persons engaged in massage and massage establishments and inspect the license of
practitioners and establishments for compliance. The refusal of a practitioner or
establishment to permit inspections is grounds for revocation, suspension, or refusal to
issue a license pursuant to this part.
63-33-205. Exempted persons.
This part does not affect, prevent, or restrict:
(1) Persons qualified and licensed to practice other health professions
from engaging in the practice of massage when incidental to the practice of their
profession;
- 93 - 012037

(2) Persons qualified and licensed to practice as barbers or
cosmetologists from engaging in the practice of massage when incidental to the
practice of their profession;
(3) Students enrolled in an institution described in § 63-33-203(a)(1) or a
public school of this state; provided, that the student does not hold the student's
self out as a licensed massage therapist and does not receive compensation for
massage; and
(4) Massage therapists licensed in other states or countries when
providing educational programs or services for a period of time not to exceed
thirty (30) days within a calendar year.
63-33-206. Temporary license.
(a) The commissioner may, in the commissioner's discretion, grant a temporary
license to a person who has been licensed, registered, or certified, in good standing, in
another state, territory of the United States, or the District of Columbia, that meets all
other requirements for reciprocity under this chapter and rules promulgated pursuant to
this chapter, but which does not require successful passage of a competency
examination approved by the commissioner.
(b) A person granted a temporary license pursuant to this section may work if
the person is at all times working under the supervision of a person licensed pursuant to
§ 63-33-203.
(c)
(1) A temporary license issued pursuant to this section expires six (6)
months after the date of issuance.
(2) A person granted a temporary license pursuant to this section may
apply for one (1) extension of the person's temporary license for an additional six
(6) months if:
(A)
- 94 - 012037

(i) The person has been unable to take a competency
exam approved by the commissioner within the initial temporary
license period; and
(ii) Is registered to take an upcoming competency exam
approved by the commissioner; or
(B) The person is still waiting for the results of the most recent
competency exam approved by the commissioner.
63-33-207. Massage deemed medically therapeutic – Taxation.
Notwithstanding a law to the contrary, the act of a duly licensed massage
therapist in performing a massage is deemed to be medically therapeutic in nature and
not subject to the collection of any form of state or local taxation regulations not also
imposed on other medically therapeutic activities.
63-33-208. Designation as "primary care provider" prohibited.
A person licensed by the commissioner under this part must not be referred to as
a primary care provider or permitted to use such designation.
63-33-209. Powers and duties of commissioner – Passage rate of schools of
massage therapy.
In addition to the powers and duties granted to or imposed by this chapter, the
commissioner has the following powers and duties:
(1) To prescribe the minimum curricular and minimum standards for
schools of massage therapy and for courses of training that prepare individuals
for licensure under this part;
(2) To approve such schools and courses as meet the requirements of
this part and the rules of the commissioner;
(3) To issue certificates of approval to such schools and courses that
meet the requirements of this part and the rules of the commissioner;
- 95 - 012037

(4) To conduct hearings for disciplinary action against schools or courses
that fail to meet the minimum requirements of this part and the rules of the
commissioner; and
(5) To annually publish passage rates for each school of massage
therapy, based upon the results of each student's success in taking a national
examination approved by the commissioner. Schools that fail to achieve an
overall passing rate of seventy percent (70%) are required to submit a remedial
plan to be approved by the commissioner.
63-33-210. Alternative licensure process.
(a) The commissioner may issue a license to practice massage therapy to an
applicant who:
(1) Meets the qualifications set forth in § 63-33-103; and
(2) Has been certified by the National Certification Board for Therapeutic
Massage and Bodywork for the five-year period immediately preceding
application for licensure and can submit documentation satisfactory to the
commissioner that the applicant has engaged in the practice of massage therapy
in another state for the five-year period immediately preceding application for
licensure, and who either:
(A) Has met the qualifications set forth in § 63-33-203(a), but is
unable, because the educational institution either was not state approved
or is no longer in existence, to produce a transcript to document
compliance; or
(B) Graduated from a qualified massage school or course prior to
October 1, 1995.
(b) The commissioner may promulgate rules that are necessary to effectuate this
section.
- 96 - 012037

SECTION 71. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-301. Part definitions.
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Athletic injury" means an injury sustained by a person as a result of
the person's participation in exercises, sports, games, or recreation requiring
physical strength, agility, flexibility, range of motion, speed, or stamina, or
comparable athletic injury that prevents the person from participating in such
activities; and
(2) "Athletic trainer" means a person with specific qualifications as set
forth in this part, who, upon the advice, consent, and oral or written prescriptions
or referrals of a physician licensed under this title, carries out the practice of
prevention, recognition, evaluation, management, disposition, treatment, or
rehabilitation of athletic injuries, and, in carrying out these functions, the athletic
trainer may use physical modalities, such as heat, light, sound, cold, electricity,
or mechanical devices related to prevention, recognition, evaluation,
management, disposition, rehabilitation, and treatment; an athletic trainer shall
practice only in those areas in which such athletic trainer is competent by reason
of training or experience that can be substantiated by records or other evidence
found acceptable by the board in the exercise of the commissioner's considered
discretion.
63-33-302. Prohibited representations as an athletic trainer.
(a) A person shall not represent the person's self as, or claim to be, an athletic
trainer or perform, for compensation, any of the activities of an athletic trainer without
first obtaining a license under this part.
(b) This part does not prevent a person from serving as a student-trainer, or a
similar position, if such service is not primarily for compensation and is carried out under
- 97 - 012037

the supervision of an athletic trainer duly licensed as provided in this part and a
physician licensed under this title. Such supervision must be provided under the
guidelines of the National Athletic Trainers' Association (NATA) Board of Certification,
Inc., or approved by the commissioner.
63-33-303. Documentation required from applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for an athletic trainer
license shall provide documentation in the form required by the commissioner that the
applicant:
(1) Has met the athletic training curriculum requirements of a college or
university approved by the commissioner; and
(2) Has satisfactorily completed all of the National Athletic Trainers'
Association (NATA) Board of Certification, Inc., qualifications and is certified as
an athletic trainer in good standing by the NATA Board of Certification, Inc., or
approved by the commissioner.
63-33-304. Exempted persons.
(a) This part does not limit or prevent a person duly licensed or certified under
the laws of this state from practicing the profession for which the person was licensed or
certified.
(b) This part does not apply to a person engaging in the practice of athletic
training while employed for such purpose by a postsecondary educational institution or
professional athletic organization from another state that is temporarily present in this
state for an athletic competition or exhibition.
(c) This part does not apply to physicians duly licensed under this title who
employ or contract for services provided by persons in the physician's office assisting in
the care of patients and rendered under the supervision, control, and responsibility of the
licensed physician.
63-33-305. Civil penalties.
- 98 - 012037

The commissioner has the authority to assess civil penalties commensurate with
those assessable under § 63-1-134 against persons who have knowingly employed,
contracted for, or otherwise utilized unlicensed persons in the practice of athletic
training, with or without compensation.
63-33-306. Athletic trainers – Scope of practice.
(a) An athletic trainer may use dry needling, as defined in § 63-33-1602, and
physical modalities, such as heat, light, sound, cold, electricity, or mechanical devices,
for the prevention, recognition, evaluation, management, disposition, rehabilitation, and
treatment of athletic injuries.
(b) An athletic trainer shall only practice in those areas in which an athletic
trainer is competent by reason of training or experience that can be substantiated by
records or other evidence found acceptable by the board in the exercise of the
commissioner's considered discretion.
(c) An athletic trainer shall obtain such training and certification in the practice of
dry needling as the commissioner may require by rule. The practice of dry needling by
an athletic trainer under this chapter does not constitute the practice of acupuncture
under part 4 of this chapter.
(d) The commissioner is authorized to promulgate rules to effectuate this
section. The rules must be promulgated in accordance with the Uniform Administrative
Procedures Act, compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
SECTION 72. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-401. Part definitions.
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "ACAOM" means the Accreditation Commission for Acupuncture and
Oriental Medicine;
- 99 - 012037

(2) "Acupuncture" means a form of health care developed from traditional
and modern oriental medical concepts that employs oriental medical diagnosis
and treatment and adjunctive therapies and diagnostic techniques for the
promotion, maintenance, and restoration of health and the prevention of disease.
"Adjunctive therapies" within the scope of "acupuncture" may include
acupressure, cupping, thermal, and electrical treatment and the recommendation
of dietary guidelines and supplements and therapeutic exercise based on
traditional oriental medical concepts;
(3) "ADS" means an acupuncture detoxification specialist trained in, and
who performs only, the five-point auricular detoxification treatment;
(4) "NADA" means the National Acupuncture Detoxification Association;
(5) "NCCAOM" means the National Certification Commission for
Acupuncture and Oriental Medicine; and
(6) "Practice of acupuncture" means the insertion of acupuncture needles
and the application of moxibustion to specific areas of the human body based on
oriental medical diagnosis as a primary mode of therapy.
63-33-402. Exempted persons – Unlawful practice of acupuncture – Limited
licensure.
(a) This part does not apply to:
(1) Physicians licensed under chapter 6 or chapter 9 of this title, and
does not prevent the practice of acupuncture by such physicians or to prevent
such physicians from using the title "acupuncturist";
(2) Registered nurses who are nationally certified as holistic nurses and
who have successfully completed an accredited education program in
acupuncture; or
(3) Chiropractic physicians licensed under chapter 4 of this title, and
does not prevent the practice of acupuncture by chiropractic physicians who
- 100 - 012037

have completed two hundred fifty (250) hours of an accredited acupuncture
course and have passed the National Board of Chiropractic Examiners
acupuncture exam.
(b) It is otherwise unlawful to practice acupuncture for compensation or
gratuitously unless licensed under this part. This restriction does not apply to the
following:
(1) Students practicing acupuncture under the supervision of a licensed
acupuncturist as part of a course of study approved by the commissioner; or
(2) Individuals who do not otherwise possess the credentials required for
the practice of acupuncture by this part, or rules promulgated under this part, by
the commissioner are granted limited licensure as an ADS for the purpose of the
treatment of alcoholism, substance abuse, or chemical dependency if they meet
the following conditions:
(A) Provide documentation of successful completion of a
commissioner-approved training program in auricular detoxification
acupuncture that meets or exceeds standards of training set by NADA;
(B) Practice auricular detoxification treatment in a hospital, clinic,
or treatment facility that provides comprehensive alcohol and substance
abuse or chemical dependency services, including counseling, under the
supervision of a licensed acupuncturist or medical director;
(C) Satisfy all appropriate ethical standards; and
(D) Limit their practice to the five-point auricular detoxification
treatment.
63-33-403. Documentation required from applicants.
(a) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as
an acupuncturist shall provide documentation in the form required by the commissioner
that the applicant:
- 101 - 012037

(1) Has successfully completed a three-year postsecondary training
program or acupuncture college program that is ACAOM-accredited or in
candidacy status or that meets ACAOM's standards;
(2) Has successfully completed an NCCAOM-approved clean needle
technique course; and
(3) Either:
(A) Has current active status as a diplomate in acupuncture of the
NCCAOM; or
(B) Has current state licensure in good standing by another state
with substantially equivalent or higher standards.
(b) The commissioner shall issue a limited acupuncture license to an ADS who
meets the requirements listed in § 63-33-402(b)(2).
63-33-404. License renewals.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-105, in order to renew a license, a
person shall submit proof of current active NCCAOM certification in acupuncture or
document compliance with § 63-33-403. To renew an ADS license, a person shall
submit proof of current active practice in auricular detoxification treatment, as
determined by the commissioner.
63-33-405. Health practices.
(a) All licensed individuals under this part shall use only presterilized, disposable
needles in their administration of acupuncture treatments. The use of staples in the
practice of acupuncture is prohibited.
(b) Health practices must include:
(1) Hands being washed with soap and water or other disinfectant before
handling needles and between treatment of different patients;
(2) Skin in the area of penetration being thoroughly swabbed with alcohol
or other germicidal solution before inserting needles; and
- 102 - 012037

(3) Individuals passing a nationally recognized clean needle technique
course before being allowed to practice acupuncture and related techniques.
63-33-406. Use of titles "licensed acupuncturist" or "ADS".
The titles "licensed acupuncturist" or "ADS" may be used by persons licensed
under this part. A person who is not properly licensed to practice medicine or
osteopathic medicine shall not use licensure under this part to identify the person as a
doctor or physician.
SECTION 73. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-501. Practice of art therapy.
(a) The practice of art therapy in this state is declared to affect the public health,
safety, and welfare of citizens of this state.
(b) The commissioner is authorized to protect the public from:
(1) The practice of art therapy by unqualified persons; and
(2) Unprofessional, unethical, and harmful conduct by art therapy
practitioners.
(c) A person shall not represent to be or function as a professional art therapist
in this state unless the person holds a valid license issued by the commissioner. The
commissioner shall also regulate the practice of art therapy.
63-33-502. Part definitions.
As used in this part:
(1) "Appraisal activities":
(A) Means selecting, administering, scoring, and interpreting art
therapy instruments that are used to understand, measure, or facilitate an
individual's normal human growth and development; and
(B) Does not include the use of projective techniques in the
assessment of personality, nor the use of psychological or clinical tests
- 103 - 012037

designed to identify or classify abnormal or pathological human behavior,
nor the use of individually administered intelligence tests;
(2) "Art therapy" means the integrated application of psychotherapeutic
principles and methods with specialized training in visual art media, the
neurobiological implications of art-making and the creative process, and art-
based assessment models to assist individuals, families, or groups to improve
mental functioning, increase self-awareness and self-esteem, resolve conflicts
and distress, and enhance social functioning;
(3) "Art therapy certified supervisor" means a person credentialed by the
Art Therapy Credentials Board, Inc., to provide supervised clinical experience for
an associate art therapist;
(4) "Associate art therapist" means a person holding a master's or
doctoral degree in art therapy while engaged in the practice of professional art
therapy under supervision as part of clinical training to fulfill the supervised
experience requirement for becoming a licensed professional art therapist;
(5) "Certified art therapist" means a person holding national board
certification (ATR-BC) from the Art Therapy Credentials Board, Inc.;
(6) "Credentialed art therapist" means a person holding credentials in
good standing with the Art Therapy Credentials Board, Inc., as a registered art
therapist (ATR), certified art therapist (ATR-BC), or art therapy certified
supervisor;
(7) "Licensed professional art therapist" means a person who is licensed
to practice professional art therapy in this state;
(8) "Practice of professional art therapy":
(A) Means rendering or offering to render to individuals, groups,
organizations, or the general public any service as an independent or
- 104 - 012037

adjunctive therapist involving the application of art therapy principles,
techniques, methods, or procedures; and
(B) Includes, but is not limited to, therapeutic interventions to
facilitate alternative modes of receptive and expressive communication,
development of treatment plans, appraisal activities, consulting and
referral activities, and prevention and treatment of mental and emotional
conditions; and
(9) "Supervision" means the regular observation and oversight of the
functions and activities of a graduate art therapy student as part of an internship
or practicum experience, or an associate art therapist engaged in the practice of
art therapy to fulfill the requirements for licensure under § 63-33-503.
63-33-503. Documentation required from applicants.
(a) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure
under this part shall provide documentation in the form required by the commissioner
that the applicant has:
(1) Passed the board certification examination of the Art Therapy
Credentials Board, Inc.; and
(2) Either:
(A) Received a master's degree or doctoral degree in art therapy
from a program approved by the American Art Therapy Association or
accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of Allied Health Education
Programs at the time the degree was conferred, and has completed no
less than one thousand (1,000) client contact hours of experience after
the master's degree was conferred under the supervision of an art
therapy certified supervisor, licensed professional art therapist,
credentialed art therapist, or other licensed mental health professional
approved by the commissioner. At least one-half (1/2) of the required
- 105 - 012037

supervision hours must be provided by an art therapy certified supervisor,
licensed professional art therapist, or certified art therapist; or
(B) Received a master's degree or doctoral degree from a college
or university that was accredited by a national or regional accrediting
organization recognized by the Council for Higher Education Accreditation
in a program with a graduate-level course of study and clinical training
that, as determined by the commissioner, is equivalent to an approved or
accredited program in art therapy, and has completed not less than one
thousand five hundred (1,500) hours of client contact experience after the
qualifying degree was conferred under the supervision of an art therapy
certified supervisor, licensed professional art therapist, credentialed art
therapist, or other licensed mental health professional approved by the
commissioner. At least one-half (1/2) of the required supervision hours
must be provided by an art therapy certified supervisor, licensed
professional art therapist, or certified art therapist.
(b) A person holding a national credential in good standing as a certified art
therapist is deemed to have met the requirements of this section upon submitting an
application and fee and providing evidence satisfying the requirements of § 63-33-103 in
the form required by the commissioner.
63-33-504. Use of title "licensed professional art therapist" or "licensed art
therapist."
(a) A person shall not use the title "licensed professional art therapist" or
"licensed art therapist," or use an abbreviation to indicate or imply that the person is a
licensed professional art therapist in this state unless the person holds a license issued
by the commissioner under this part. This subsection (a) does not prohibit an associate
art therapist from using the title "associate art therapist" in accordance with this part.
(b) A person shall not practice professional art therapy unless the person is:
- 106 - 012037

(1) Licensed by the commissioner as a licensed professional art
therapist;
(2) An associate art therapist, as long as the person uses the title of
"associate art therapist" and does not represent themselves to the public as a
licensed professional art therapist; or
(3) Exempt from licensure under § 63-33-506.
63-33-505. Authorized work settings.
(a) A licensed professional art therapist may practice independently for and with
organizations that include, but are not limited to, addiction and rehabilitation centers, art
studios and centers, behavioral health hospitals and outpatient settings, cancer
treatment centers, community centers, community services boards, correctional facilities,
disability services, eating disorder clinics, government agencies, medical hospitals and
outpatient settings, military bases and veterans and family services, museums,
nonprofits, nursing homes, physical rehabilitation, residential treatment centers, schools,
senior living facilities, state programs, and wellness centers.
(b) Until the commissioner promulgates rules to establish the requirements for
private outpatient independent practice by a licensed professional art therapist, a
licensed professional art therapist shall only work in a private, outpatient independent
setting if the patient is referred to the therapist by:
(1) A physician licensed under chapter 6 or 9 of this title;
(2) A psychologist licensed under chapter 11 of this title;
(3) A professional counselor licensed under chapter 33, part 18 of this
title;
(4) A professional counselor designated as a mental health service
provider under chapter 33, part 18 of this title;
(5) A marital and family therapist licensed under chapter 33, part 18 of
this title;
- 107 - 012037

(6) A pastoral counselor licensed under chapter 33, part 18 of this title;
(7) A licensed master's social worker licensed under chapter 23 of this
title;
(8) A licensed clinical social worker licensed under chapter 23 of this title;
or
(9) Another advanced medical or mental health professional licensed
under this title, as determined by the commissioner.
63-33-506. Authorized activities.
(a) This part does not:
(1) Require licensure or restrict the activities of a student enrolled in a
graduate program in art therapy approved by the commissioner while practicing
art therapy under qualified supervision and as part of an approved course of
study; or
(2) Prohibit or restrict the practice of persons authorized to practice under
this title who perform services consistent with the scope of practice of their
profession and within the scope of their training and competence if the persons
do not represent themselves to the public as a professional art therapist or as
holding a license issued under this part.
(b) This part does not permit any method of treatment that involves the
administration or prescription of drugs or the practice of medicine in this state or permits
a person licensed as a professional art therapist to perform psychological testing.
(c) Subsection (b) does not prohibit a licensed professional art therapist from
conducting appraisal activities. Consistent with each licensed professional art therapist's
formal education and training, licensed professional art therapists may administer and
utilize appropriate art therapy assessment instruments that measure or determine
problems or dysfunctions within the context of human growth and development as part of
the therapeutic process or in the development of a treatment plan.
- 108 - 012037

SECTION 74. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-601. Practice of music therapy.
(a) The practice of music therapy in this state is declared to affect the public
health, safety, and welfare of citizens of this state.
(b) The commissioner is authorized and given the duty to protect the public from:
(1) The practice of clinical music therapy by unqualified persons; and
(2) Unprofessional, unethical, and harmful conduct by music therapy
practitioners.
(c) A person shall not represent to be or function as a professional music
therapist in this state unless the person holds a valid license issued by the
commissioner. The commissioner shall also regulate the practice of music therapy.
(d) This part does not restrict the non-clinical, non-therapeutic music intervention
of the Tennessee person-centered music program administered by the Tennessee
commission on aging and disability, created by § 52-8-102, and associated area
agencies on aging and disability or their representatives.
63-33-602. Part definitions.
As used in this part:
(1) "Certified professional music therapist" means a person certified to
practice music therapy under this part;
(2) "Music intervention" means the use of music in an individualized
approach that includes music improvisation, receptive music listening, song
writing, lyric discussion, music and imagery, singing, music performance,
learning through music, music combined with other arts, music-assisted
relaxation, music-based education, electronic music technology, adapted music
intervention, and movement to music, that may be used in a clinical, therapeutic
relationship or in a non-clinical, nontherapeutic manner; and
- 109 - 012037

(3) "Music therapy":
(A) Means the clinical and evidence-based use of music
interventions to accomplish individualized goals for people of all ages and
ability levels within a therapeutic relationship by a board-certified music
therapist; and
(B) Does not include the screening, diagnosis, or assessment of
any physical, mental, or communication disorder.
63-33-603. Rules.
In addition to the authority granted by and requirements found in part 1 of this
chapter, the rules promulgated by the commissioner for the implementation of this part
must:
(1) Provide for the requirements for licensure as set forth in § 63-33-604;
and
(2) Take into consideration the standards of ethics and professional
conduct of the code of ethics of the American Music Therapy Association and
code of professional ethics of the Certification Board for Music Therapists in
effect on January 1, 2025, or any successor organization.
63-33-604. Documentation required from applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, the applicant shall provide
documentation in the form required by the commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Holds a bachelor's degree or higher in music therapy, or its
equivalent, including clinical training hours from a music therapy program within
an accredited college or university;
(2) Has passed the examination for board certification offered by the
Certification Board for Music Therapists, or any successor organization, or
provides proof of being transitioned into board certification; and
(3) Is currently a board-certified music therapist.
- 110 - 012037

63-33-605. Use of title "certified professional music therapist" or "certified music
therapist."
(a) A person shall not use the title "certified professional music therapist," or
"certified music therapist," or use any abbreviation to indicate that the person is certified
as a professional music therapist in this state unless the person holds a certificate
issued by the commissioner under this part.
(b) Subsection (a) does not prohibit:
(1) A person who is licensed, certified, or regulated under the laws of this
state in another profession or occupation, including physicians, psychologists,
psychoanalysts, registered nurses, marriage and family therapists, social
workers, occupational therapists, professional or rehabilitation counselors,
speech-language pathologists or audiologists, or personnel supervised by a
licensed professional from performing work, including the use of music, that is
incidental to the practice of the person's licensed, certified, or regulated
profession or occupation, if the person does not represent themself as a music
therapist;
(2) A person whose training and national certification attests to the
person's preparation and ability to practice their certified profession or
occupation, if the person does not represent themself as a music therapist;
(3) A practice of music therapy as an integral part of a program of study
for students enrolled in an accredited music therapy program, if the student does
not represent themself as a music therapist;
(4) A person who practices music therapy under the supervision of a
certified professional music therapist, if the person does not represent themself
as a music therapist; or
(5) The use of music intervention in a non-clinical, non-therapeutic
manner by persons who do not represent themselves as music therapists or
- 111 - 012037

through a program that is not represented to be a music therapy program,
including the Tennessee person-centered music program administered by the
Tennessee commission on aging and disability, created by § 52-8-102.
63-33-606. Authorized work settings – Required reviews.
(a) A certified professional music therapist may practice independently for and
with organizations that include, but are not limited to, addiction and rehabilitation
centers, music studios and centers, behavioral health hospitals and outpatient settings,
cancer treatment centers, community centers, community services boards, correctional
facilities, disability services, eating disorder clinics, government agencies, medical
hospitals and outpatient settings, military bases and veterans and family services,
museums, nonprofits, nursing homes, physical rehabilitation, residential treatment
centers, schools, senior living facilities, state programs, and wellness centers.
(b)
(1)
(A) Before a certified professional music therapist provides music
therapy services to a client for an identified clinical or developmental
need, the certified professional music therapist shall review the client's
diagnosis, treatment needs, and treatment plan with the healthcare
providers involved in the client's care.
(B) During the provision of music therapy services to a client, the
certified professional music therapist shall collaborate, as applicable, with
the client's treatment team, including the client's physician, psychologist,
licensed clinical social worker, or other mental health professional.
During the provision of music therapy services to a client with a
communication disorder, the certified professional music therapist shall
collaborate and discuss the music therapy treatment plan with the client's
- 112 - 012037

audiologist or speech-Ianguage pathologist so that a music therapist may
work with the client and address communication skills.
(2) Before a certified professional music therapist provides music therapy
services to a student for an identified educational need in a special education
setting, the certified professional music therapist shall review the student's
diagnosis, treatment needs, and treatment plan with the individualized family
service plan or individualized education program team.
(3) When providing educational or healthcare services, a certified
professional music therapist shall not replace the services provided by an
audiologist or a speech-language pathologist. Unless authorized to practice
speech-language pathology, music therapists shall not evaluate, examine, or
provide instruction or counsel on speech, language, communication, and
swallowing disorders and conditions. A person certified as a professional music
therapist shall not represent to the public that the person is authorized to treat a
communication disorder. This subdivision (b)(3) does not prohibit a person,
certified as a professional music therapist from representing to the public that the
person is qualified to work with clients with communication disorders and to
address communication skills.
63-33-607. Authorized activities.
In addition to any other authority granted under this part, certified professional
music therapists may:
(1) Accept referrals for music therapy services from medical,
developmental, mental health, or education professionals; family members;
clients; caregivers; or others involved with and authorized to provide client
services;
(2) Conduct a music therapy assessment of a client to determine if
treatment is indicated. If treatment is indicated, then the certified professional
- 113 - 012037

music therapist may collect systematic, comprehensive, and accurate information
to determine the appropriateness and type of music therapy services to provide
for the client;
(3) Develop an individualized music therapy treatment plan for the client
that is based upon the results of the music therapy assessment. The music
therapy treatment plan must include individualized goals and objectives that
focus on the assessed needs and strengths of the client and specify the music
therapy approaches and interventions to be used to address these goals and
objectives;
(4) Implement an individualized music therapy treatment plan that is
consistent with any other developmental, rehabilitative, habilitative, medical,
mental health, preventive, wellness care, or educational services being provided
to the client;
(5) Evaluate a client's response to music therapy and the music therapy
treatment plan, documenting change and progress, and suggesting
modifications, as appropriate;
(6) Develop a plan for determining when the provision of music therapy
services is no longer needed in collaboration with the client, physician, or other
provider of health care or education of the client, family members of the client,
and any other appropriate person upon whom the client relies for support;
(7) Minimize barriers to ensure that the client receives music therapy
services in the least restrictive environment;
(8) Collaborate with and educate the client and the family, caregiver of
the client, or any other appropriate person regarding the needs of the client that
are being addressed in music therapy and the manner in which the music
therapy treatment addresses those needs; and
- 114 - 012037

(9) Utilize their appropriate knowledge and skills to practice, which
include the use of research, reasoning, and problem-solving skills in determining
appropriate actions in the context of each clinical setting.
63-33-608. Psychological practice.
This part does not permit a certified professional music therapist to engage in a
psychological practice as described in chapter 11, part 2 of this title.
SECTION 75. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-701. Part definitions.
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Dietetics/nutrition practice":
(A) Means the integration and application of scientific principles of
food, nutrition, biochemistry, physiology, management, and behavioral
and social sciences in achieving and maintaining health through the life
cycle and in the treatment of disease; and
(B) Includes nutritional assessment, development,
implementation, and evaluation of nutrition care plans, nutritional
counseling and education, and the development and administration of
nutrition care standards and systems;
(2) "Dietitian" and "nutritionist" may be used interchangeably; and
(3) "Dietitian/nutritionist" means a healthcare professional engaging in
dietetics/nutrition practice and licensed under this part.
63-33-702. Use of titles – Exempted persons.
(a) It is unlawful for any person to engage in the practice of dietetics/nutrition, to
act or represent the person to be a dietitian or a nutritionist or to use such titles as
"dietitian/nutritionist," "licensed dietitian," "licensed nutritionist," or such letters as "L.D.,"
"L.N.," or any facsimile thereof, or any word, letters, or title indicating or implying that
- 115 - 012037

such person is a dietitian/nutritionist, unless the person holds a license and otherwise
complies with this chapter and the rules adopted by the commissioner.
(b) This part does not affect, prevent, or restrict:
(1) Persons qualified and licensed to practice other health professions
from engaging in the practice of dietetics/nutrition when incidental to the practice
of their profession. This part does not apply to persons licensed to practice
medicine or osteopathic medicine pursuant to chapters 6 and 9 of this title;
(2) Students enrolled in an approved academic program in dietetics, if
such practice constitutes a part of a supervised course of study and such student
is designated by title clearly indicating such student's status as a student or
trainee;
(3) A dietitian serving in the armed forces or the public health service of
the United States or employed by the veterans administration from engaging in
the practice of dietetics if such practice is related to such service or employment;
(4) Persons performing the activities and services of a nutrition educator
in the employment of a federal, state, county, or municipal agency or an
elementary or secondary school or accredited degree-granting educational
institution if such activities and services are part of a salaried position;
(5) Federal, state, county, or local employees involved with nutrition-
related programs, including, but not limited to, the cooperative extension service,
child nutrition programs, and Project Head Start from engaging in the practice of
dietetics/nutrition within the discharge of their official duties if the person
engaging in dietetic/nutrition practice outside the scope of such official duty is
licensed as provided in this section;
(6) Persons employed in a hospital or nursing home as defined in § 68-
11-201 and subject to licensure by the board for licensing health care facilities; or
(7)
- 116 - 012037

(A) Persons who do not hold themselves out to be licensed or
registered dietitians/nutritionists of the right to provide services and
information related to nonmedical nutrition while:
(1) Employed by or operating a health weight loss or
fitness program;
(2) Employed by or operating a health food store;
(3) Employed by or operating a business that sells health
products, including dietary supplements, food or food materials, or
provides nonmedical nutritional information or distributes
nutritional literature; or
(4) Conducting classes or disseminating information
related to nonmedical nutrition.
(B) As used in this subdivision (b)(7), "nonmedical" means
engaging in a practice that does not constitute the practice of medicine,
osteopathic medicine, chiropractic, dentistry, or podiatry.
63-33-703. Therapeutic dietary regimen.
A therapeutic dietary regimen must not be developed unless pursuant to the
appropriate orders or referral of practitioners licensed as medical or osteopathic
physicians, dentists, chiropractors, podiatrists, physician assistants, or advanced
practice registered nurses, when incidental to the practice of their respective
professions.
63-33-704. Documentation required from applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
dietitian/nutritionist shall provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Has received a baccalaureate or post-baccalaureate degree from a
regionally accredited college or university that provides a major course of study
- 117 - 012037

in human nutrition, food and nutrition, dietetics, or food systems management, or
an equivalent major course of study as approved by the commissioner;
(2) Has successfully completed a planned continuous preprofessional
experience in nutrition practice of no less than nine hundred (900) hours under
the supervision of a registered dietitian, or successfully completed a program of
supervised clinical experience approved by the commission on dietetic
registration of the American Dietetic Association; and
(3) Has passed the national examination prepared and administered by
the commission on dietetic registration of the American Dietetic Association.
63-33-705. Temporary permits.
(a) The commissioner may, in the commissioner's discretion, issue temporary
permits to engage in dietetics/nutrition practice to an applicant upon submission of
satisfactory evidence that the person:
(A) Has successfully completed the academic and experiential
requirements to be licensed as a dietitian/nutritionist;
(B) Has applied for or taken a licensing examination;
(C) Is awaiting notification of examination results; and
(D) Has paid the fee required for temporary permits.
(b) Temporary permits expire one (1) year from the date of issuance and may be
renewed for a period not to exceed six (6) months upon submitting to the commissioner
a satisfactory explanation of the applicant's failure to become licensed within the one-
year term.
SECTION 76. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-801. Part definitions – Setting for practice of polysomnography.
(a) As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
- 118 - 012037

(1) "Direct supervision" means that the polysomnographic technologist
providing supervision must be present in the area where the polysomnographic
procedure is being performed and immediately available to furnish assistance
and direction throughout the performance of the procedure;
(2) "General supervision" means that the polysomnographic procedure is
provided under a physician's overall direction and control, but the physician's
presence is not required during the performance of the procedure;
(3) "Polysomnographic student" means a person who is enrolled in an
educational program that is accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of
Allied Health Education Programs (CAAHEP), as provided in § 63-33-803(a)(1),
and who may provide sleep-related services under the direct supervision of a
polysomnographic technologist as a part of the person's educational program;
(4) "Polysomnographic technician" means a person who has graduated
from an accredited educational program described in § 63-33-803(a)(1) but has
not yet passed the national certifying examination given by the Board of
Registered Polysomnographic Technologists, who has obtained a temporary
permit from the commissioner, and who may provide sleep-related services
under the general supervision of a licensed physician;
(5) "Polysomnographic technologist" means a person who is credentialed
by the Board of Registered Polysomnographic Technologists and is licensed by
the commissioner to engage in the practice of polysomnography under the
general supervision of a licensed physician;
(6) "Polysomnographic trainee" means a person who is enrolled in an
accredited sleep technologist education program (A-STEP) that is accredited by
the American Academy of Sleep Medicine and who may provide sleep-related
services under the direct supervision of a polysomnographic technologist as a
part of the person's educational program;
- 119 - 012037

(7) "Practice of polysomnography" means the staging and scoring of
sleep by continuous and simultaneous monitoring of the stages of sleep and
wake through use of an electroencephalogram (EEG), an electrooculogram
(EOG), and a submental electromyogram (EMG), in conjunction with the
recording and monitoring of other physiological variables, and the assignment of
values for duration, frequency, and type of event to each stage of sleep in which
the event occurred. The following tasks are considered a part of the practice of
polysomnography only when performed as part of the staging and scoring of
sleep under the general supervision of a licensed physician:
(A) Monitoring and recording physiologic data during the
evaluation of sleep-related disorders, including sleep-related respiratory
disturbances, by applying the following techniques, equipment, and
procedures:
(i) Continuous or bilevel positive airway pressure titration
on spontaneously breathing patients using a mask or oral
appliance when the mask or oral appliance does not extend into
the trachea or attach to an artificial airway;
(ii) Supplemental low flow oxygen therapy of less than six
(6) liters per minute, utilizing nasal cannula or continuous or
bilevel positive airway pressure during a polysomnogram;
(iii) Capnography during a polysomnogram;
(iv) Cardiopulmonary resuscitation;
(v) Pulse oximetry;
(vi) Gastroesophageal pH monitoring;
(vii) Esophageal pressure monitoring;
- 120 - 012037

(viii) Sleep staging, including surface
electroencephalography, surface electrooculography, and surface
submental electromyography;
(ix) Surface electromyography;
(x) Electrocardiography;
(xi) Respiratory effort monitoring, including thoracic and
abdominal movement;
(xii) Plethysmography blood flow monitoring;
(xiii) Snore monitoring;
(xiv) Audio or video monitoring;
(xv) Body movement monitoring;
(xvi) Nocturnal penile tumescence monitoring;
(xvii) Nasal and oral airflow monitoring;
(xviii) Body temperature monitoring; and
(xiv) Monitoring the effects that a mask or oral appliance
used to treat sleep disorders has on sleep patterns; however, the
mask or oral appliance must not extend into the trachea or attach
to an artificial airway;
(B) Observing and monitoring physical signs and symptoms,
general behavior, and general physical response to polysomnographic
evaluation and determining whether initiation, modification, or
discontinuation of a treatment regimen is warranted;
(C) Analyzing and scoring data collected during the monitoring
described in subdivisions (a)(7)(A) and (B) for the purpose of assisting a
licensed physician in the diagnosis and treatment of sleep and wake
disorders that result from developmental defects, the aging process,
physical injury, disease, or actual or anticipated somatic dysfunction;
- 121 - 012037

(D) Implementation of a written or verbal order from a licensed
physician that requires the practice of polysomnography; and
(E) Education of a patient regarding the treatment regimen that
assists the patient in improving the patient's sleep; and
(8) "Sleep-related services" means acts performed by polysomnographic
technicians, polysomnographic trainees, polysomnographic students, and other
persons permitted to perform those services under this part, in a setting
described in subsection (c) that would be considered the practice of
polysomnography if performed by a polysomnographic technologist.
(b) A licensed dentist shall make or direct the making and use of any oral
appliance used to treat sleep disordered breathing and shall evaluate the structures of
the patient's oral and maxillofacial region for purposes of fitting the appliance.
(c) The practice of polysomnography must take place only in a hospital, a stand-
alone sleep laboratory or sleep center, or in the patient's home in accordance with a
physician's order; however, the scoring of data and the education of patients may take
place in settings other than in a sleep laboratory, sleep center, or the patient's home.
63-33-802. Exemptions.
(a) This part does not limit or restrict a healthcare practitioner licensed under this
title from engaging in the full scope of practice of the person's profession.
(b) This part does not apply to diagnostic electroencephalograms conducted in
accordance with the guidelines of the American Clinical Neurophysiology Society.
63-33-803. Documentation required from applicants – License renewals.
(a) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure
under this part shall provide documentation in the form required by the commissioner
that the applicant:
(1) Meets one (1) of the following educational requirements:
- 122 - 012037

(A) Graduation from a polysomnographic educational program
that is accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of Allied Health
Education Programs;
(B) Graduation from a respiratory care educational program that
is accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of Allied Health
Education Programs and completion of the curriculum for a
polysomnography certificate established and accredited by the
Committee on Accreditation for Respiratory Care of the Commission on
Accreditation of Allied Health Education Programs;
(C) Graduation from an electro neurodiagnostic technologist
educational program with a polysomnographic technology track that is
accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of Allied Health Education
Programs; or
(D) Successful completion of an accredited sleep technologist
educational program (A-STEP) that is accredited by the American
Academy of Sleep Medicine;
(2) Has passed the national certifying examination given by the Board of
Registered Polysomnographic Technologists;
(3) Is credentialed by the Board of Registered Polysomnographic
Technologists; and
(4) Has met any additional educational or clinical requirements
established by the commissioner.
(b) A person who was engaged in the practice of polysomnography on July 1,
2007, is eligible for licensure under this part without meeting the educational requirement
of subdivision (a)(1) if the person meets the requirements of subdivisions (a)(2)-(4).
- 123 - 012037

(c) To be eligible for renewal of a license to engage in the practice of
polysomnography, a polysomnographic technologist must continue to be credentialed by
the Board of Registered Polysomnographic Technologists.
63-33-804. Unlicensed persons authorized to provide sleep-related services.
(a) The following persons may provide sleep-related services without being
licensed as a polysomnographic technologist under this part:
(1) A polysomnographic technician who provides sleep-related services
under the general supervision of a licensed physician for a period of up to one (1)
year from the date of the person's graduation from one (1) of the accredited
programs described in § 63-33-803(a)(1). The commissioner may, in the
commissioner's sole discretion, grant a one-time extension of up to three (3)
months beyond this one-year period;
(2) A polysomnographic trainee who provides sleep-related services
under the direct supervision of a polysomnographic technologist as a part of the
person's educational program while actively enrolled in an accredited sleep
technologist educational program (A-STEP) that is accredited by the American
Academy of Sleep Medicine;
(3) A polysomnographic student who provides sleep-related services
under the direct supervision of a polysomnographic technologist as a part of the
person's educational program while actively enrolled in a polysomnographic
educational program that is accredited by the Commission on Accreditation of
Allied Health Education Programs (CAAHEP);
(4) A person who is credentialed in one (1) of the health-related fields
accepted by the Board of Registered Polysomnographic Technologists who
provides sleep-related services under the direct supervision of a
polysomnographic technologist, for a period of up to one (1) year, while obtaining
- 124 - 012037

the clinical experience necessary to be eligible to sit for the examination given by
the Board of Registered Polysomnographic Technologists; and
(5) Respiratory therapists who provide polysomnography services after
being credentialed as a registered polysomnographic technologist by the Board
of Registered Polysomnographic Technologists, or as a sleep disorders specialist
by the National Board for Respiratory Care, or have undergone a standardized,
uniform mechanism to document competency in polysomnography as approved
by the commissioner. Documentation of such a credential or of passage of this
commissioner-approved mechanism must be made available at the request of
the commissioner. Respiratory therapists are not required to have a second
license as a polysomnographic technologist.
(b) Before providing sleep-related services, a polysomnographic technician shall
obtain a temporary permit from the commissioner. While providing sleep-related
services, the technician shall wear a badge that appropriately identifies the person as a
polysomnographic technician.
(c) Before providing sleep-related services, a polysomnographic trainee shall
give notice to the commissioner that the trainee is enrolled in an A-STEP educational
program accredited by the American Academy of Sleep Medicine. Trainees shall wear a
badge that appropriately identifies the trainee as a polysomnographic trainee while
providing such services.
(d) Before providing sleep-related services, a person who is obtaining clinical
experience pursuant to subdivision (a)(4) shall give notice to the commissioner that the
person is working under the direct supervision of a polysomnographic technologist in
order to gain the experience to be eligible to sit for the examination given by the Board of
Registered Polysomnographic Technologists. The person shall wear a badge that
appropriately identifies the person while providing such services.
- 125 - 012037

(e) Polysomnographic students must not receive compensation for sleep-related
services they provide and wear badges that appropriately identify them as students.
63-33-805. Use of title "Polysomnographic technologist."
A person who is licensed to engage in the practice of polysomnography in this
state has the right to use the title "polysomnographic technologist" or the abbreviation
"PSGP." Any other person shall not use that title or abbreviation, or any other words or
letters, indicating that the person is a polysomnographic technologist.
SECTION 77. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-901. Part definitions – Authorized settings for the practice of respiratory
care – Exempted persons.
(a) As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Certified respiratory therapist" means a person licensed under this
part who has obtained and maintains the credential "certified respiratory
therapist" (CRT) or the credential "certified respiratory therapy technician"
(CRTT) from the National Board for Respiratory Care;
(2) "Practice of respiratory care":
(A)
(i) Means:
(a) Under the supervision, control, and
responsibility of a licensed physician, the therapy,
management, education and instruction, rehabilitation,
diagnostic testing evaluation, and care of patients with
deficiencies and abnormalities that affect the
cardiorespiratory system and associated aspects of other
system functions; or
- 126 - 012037

(b) Under the supervision, control, and
responsibility of a licensed physician, the performance of
cardiorespiratory research, cardiorespiratory health
promotion and disease prevention, and community
wellness and education programs;
(ii) Includes, under the supervision, control, and
responsibility of a licensed physician:
(a) The administration of pharmacologic agents
and medical gasses necessary to diagnose, implement
treatment, promote disease prevention, and provide
rehabilitation to the cardiorespiratory system; however, a
respiratory care practitioner shall not prescribe controlled
substances of any kind;
(b) The performance of specific diagnostic and
testing techniques employed in the medical management
of patients to assist in diagnosis, patient and family
education, monitoring, treatment, maintenance of patient
health status, and cardiorespiratory research, including,
but not limited to, pulmonary function testing,
hemodynamic and physiologic monitoring and diagnosis of
cardiac function, and specimen collection and analysis;
(c) The establishment and maintenance of the
airways, bronchopulmonary hygiene, and cardiopulmonary
resuscitation, and cardiac and respiratory life support; and
(d) The receipt and implementation of written and
verbal physician orders and the development and
implementation of care plans and protocols;
- 127 - 012037

(3) "Registered respiratory therapist" means a person licensed under this
part who has obtained and maintains the credential "registered respiratory
therapist" (RRT) from the National Board for Respiratory Care;
(4) "Respiratory assistant" or "assistant" means a person certified as
such pursuant to this part, who has:
(A) Received on-the-job training equivalent to at least one
thousand (1,000) hours of clinical training in respiratory care, during an
eighteen-consecutive-month period that was received under the
supervision of:
(i) A registered respiratory therapist;
(ii) A certified respiratory therapist; or
(iii) A licensed physician experienced in respiratory care;
and
(B) Passed a commissioner-approved examination for respiratory
assistants. The National Board for Respiratory Care (NBRC) entry level
examination, as provided to the board by the NBRC, by contract, is the
examination accepted by the commissioner. This examination does not
grant the respiratory assistant the NBRC credential. In addition, the
commissioner may write the commissioner's own state board examination
or contract with other national testing organizations; and
(5) "Respiratory care practitioner" means a registered respiratory
therapist, a certified respiratory therapist, or a respiratory assistant licensed
under this part.
(b) The practice of respiratory care may be performed in an inpatient or
outpatient setting, clinic, hospital, nursing home facility, private dwelling, or other place
deemed appropriate or necessary.
- 128 - 012037

(c) Registered respiratory therapists, certified respiratory therapists, and
respiratory assistants who have been issued a license or certificate by the
commissioner, pursuant to the authority of § 63-33-902, are exempt from any licensing,
certification, or permit requirements of the Tennessee Medical Laboratory Act, compiled
in title 68, chapter 29, for medical laboratory personnel or medical laboratory trainees
insofar as they engage in performing blood gases and PH analyses.
63-33-902. Licenses required – Documentation required from applicants – License
upgrades.
(a) In order to safeguard life, health, and property and promote public welfare by
requiring that only properly qualified persons practice respiratory care in this state, a
