operating expenses. Physical therapists employed by or contracting with a
- 175 - 012037

physician, physician group, as defined in accordance with the federal Physician
Self-Referral Law (42 U.S.C. § 1395nn), or entity primarily owned by physicians
and receiving wages, other compensation, or benefits pursuant to the
employment or contract are not deemed to be in violation of this part or part 1 of
this chapter solely by virtue of the employment or contract and are not subject to
licensure denial, suspension, revocation, or other disciplinary action or penalty
described under this part or part 1 of this chapter solely by virtue of the
employment or contract. This subdivision (4) does not create a prohibition on the
corporate practice of a healthcare professional where no such prohibition
previously existed;
(5) Charging unreasonable or fraudulent fees for services performed or
not performed;
(6) Making misleading, deceptive, untrue, or fraudulent representations in
violation of this part, or otherwise, in practice of the profession;
(7) Aiding or abetting a person not licensed in this state who directly or
indirectly performs activities requiring a license;
(8) Failing to report to the board an act or omission of a licensee,
applicant, or other person who violates this part;
(9) Interfering with, or refusing to cooperate in, an investigation or
disciplinary proceeding, including willful misrepresentation of facts or by the use
of threats or harassment against a patient or witness to prevent the patient or
witness from providing evidence in a disciplinary proceeding or a legal action;
(10) Failing to maintain adequate patient records that contain a minimum
of an evaluation of objective finding; a physical therapy treatment diagnosis; the
plan of care, including desired outcomes; the treatment record; a discharge plan,
including results of intervention; and sufficient information to identify the patient;
- 176 - 012037

(11) Promoting unnecessary devices, treatment intervention, or service
for the financial gain of the practitioner or of a third party;
(12) Providing treatment intervention unwarranted by the condition of the
patient, or continuing treatment beyond the point of reasonable benefit;
(13) Dividing fees or agreeing to split or divide fees received for
professional services with a person for bringing or referring a patient outside the
scope of § 63-33-1614; and
(14) Paying or accepting commissions, in any form or manner, on fees
for professional services, references, consultations, pathological reports,
prescriptions, or other services or articles supplied to patients.
63-33-1614. Required disclosures to patients – Complaints – Display of license
required.
(a) Physical therapists shall inform the patient of any financial arrangements
connected to the referral process.
(b) Physical therapists shall disclose in writing any financial interest in products
they endorse and recommend to their patients.
(c) The physical therapist has the responsibility to ensure that the patient has
knowledge of freedom of choice in services and products.
(d) Information relating to the physical therapist/patient relationship is
confidential and must not be communicated to a third party not involved in that patient's
care without the prior written consent of the patient. The physical therapist/patient
confidentiality does not extend to cases in which the physical therapist has a duty to
report information as required by law.
(e) A person may submit a complaint regarding a licensee or other person
potentially in violation of this part or part 1 of this chapter. Confidentiality must be
maintained subject to law.
- 177 - 012037

(f) The division shall keep all information relating to the receiving and
investigation of complaints filed against licensees confidential until the information
becomes public record as required by law.
(g) Each licensee shall display a copy of the licensee's license or current
renewal verification in a location accessible to public view at the licensee's place of
employment.
SECTION 83. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-1701. Short title.
This part is known and may be cited as the "Occupational Therapy Practice Act."
63-33-1702. Part definitions.
(a) As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "ACOTE" means the Accreditation Council for Occupational Therapy
Education, a nationally recognized accrediting agency for professional programs
in the field of occupational therapy;
(2) "AOTA" means the American Occupational Therapy Association;
(3) "Competence" is the application of knowledge, skills, and behaviors
required to function effectively, safely, ethically, and legally within the context of
the patient's role and environment;
(4) "Dry needling" means a skilled intervention that uses a thin filiform
needle to penetrate the skin and stimulate underlying neural, muscular, and
connective tissues for the management of neuromusculoskeletal conditions, pain,
and movement impairments;
(5) "NBCOT" means the National Board for Certification in Occupational
Therapy;
(6) "Occupational therapist" means a person licensed to engage in
occupational therapy practice under this part;
- 178 - 012037

(7) "Occupational therapy assistant" means a person licensed to assist in
occupational therapy practice under the supervision of an occupational therapist;
(8) "Occupational therapy practice":
(A) Means the therapeutic use of everyday life activities, including
occupations, for the purpose of enabling individuals or groups to
participate in roles and situations in home, school, workplace, community,
and other settings. Occupational therapy addresses the physical,
cognitive, psychosocial, and sensory aspects of performance in a variety
of contexts to support engagement in occupations that affect health, well-
being, and quality of life; and
(B) Includes:
(i) Screening, evaluation, assessment, planning,
implementation, or discharge planning in order to determine an
occupational therapy treatment diagnosis, prognosis, plan of
therapeutic intervention, or discharge plan, or to assess the
ongoing effect of intervention;
(ii) Selection and administration of standardized and
nonstandardized tests and measurements to evaluate factors
affecting activities of daily living, instrumental activities of daily
living, education, work, play, leisure, and social participation,
including:
(a) Body functions and body structures;
(b) Habits, routines, roles, and behavior patterns;
(c) Cultural, physical, environmental, social, and
spiritual context and activity demands that affect
performance; and
- 179 - 012037

(d) Performance skills, including motor, process,
and communication and interaction skills;
(iii) Methods or strategies selected to direct the process of
interventions, such as:
(a) Modification or adaptation of an activity or the
environment to enhance performance;
(b) Establishment, remediation, or restoration of a
skill or ability that has not yet developed or is impaired;
(c) Maintenance and enhancement of capabilities
without which performance in occupations would decline;
(d) Health promotion and wellness to enable or
enhance performance and safety of occupations; and
(e) Prevention of barriers to performance, including
disability prevention;
(iv) Interventions and procedures to promote or enhance
safety and performance in activities of daily living, instrumental
activities of daily living, education, work, play, leisure, and social
participation, including:
(a) Therapeutic use of occupations, exercises, and
activities;
(b) Training in self-care, self-management, home
management, and community and work reintegration;
(c) Development, remediation, or compensation of
physical, cognitive, neuromuscular, and sensory functions
and behavioral skills;
- 180 - 012037

(d) Therapeutic use of self, including an
individual's personality, insights, perceptions, and
judgments as part of the therapeutic process;
(e) Education and training of individuals, family
members, caregivers, and others;
(f) Care coordination, case management,
discharge planning, and transition services;
(g) Consulting services to groups, programs,
organizations, or communities;
(h) Assessment, recommendations, and training in
techniques and equipment to enhance functional mobility,
including wheelchair management;
(i) Driver rehabilitation and community mobility;
and
(j) Management of feeding and eating skills to
enable feeding and eating performance;
(v) Management of occupational therapy services,
including the planning, organizing, staffing, coordinating, directing,
or controlling of individuals and organizations;
(vi) Providing instruction in occupational therapy to
students in an accredited occupational therapy or occupational
therapy assistant educational program by persons who are trained
as occupational therapists or occupational therapy assistants; and
(vii) Administration, interpretation, and application of
research to occupational therapy services; and
(C) Includes specialized services provided by occupational
therapists or occupational therapy assistants who are certified or trained
- 181 - 012037

in areas of specialization that include, but are not limited to, hand therapy,
neurodevelopmental treatment, dry needling of the upper limb, sensory
integration, pediatrics, geriatrics, and neurorehabilitation, through
programs approved by AOTA or other nationally recognized
organizations;
(9) "Occupations":
(A) Means everyday life activities, named, organized, and given
value and meaning by individuals and their culture; and
(B) Includes everything that people do to occupy their time,
including caring for their needs, enjoying life, and contributing to the
social and economic fabric of their communities;
(10) "Unlicensed person," when working in occupational therapy, means
a person, often referred to as an aide, technician, transporter, or support staff,
who performs specific supportive tasks related to occupational therapy practice
under the direct supervision of an occupational therapist or an occupational
therapy assistant and whose activities do not require professional or advanced
training in the basic anatomical, biological, psychological, and social sciences
involved in the provision of occupational therapy services; and
(11) "Upper limb" means the hand, wrist, elbow, and shoulder girdle.
(b) Occupational therapy services must be provided for the purpose of promoting
health and wellness to those clients who have, or are at risk of developing, illness, injury,
disease, disorder, impairment, disability, activity limitation, or participation restriction and
may include:
(1) Training in the use of prosthetic devices;
(2) Assessment, design, development, fabrication, adaptation,
application, fitting, and training in the use of assistive technology and adaptive
and selective orthotic devices;
- 182 - 012037

(3) Application of physical agent modalities with proper training and
certification;
(4) Assessment and application of ergonomic principles;
(5) Adaptation or modification of environments, at home, work, school, or
community, and use of a range of therapeutic procedures, such as wound care
management, techniques to enhance sensory, perceptual, and cognitive
processing and manual therapy techniques, to enhance performance skills,
occupational performance, or the promotion of health and wellness; and
(6) Practice of dry needling of the upper limb, with proper training and
certification.
(c) Occupational therapy practice may occur in a variety of settings, including,
but not limited to:
(1) Institutional inpatient settings, such as acute rehabilitation facilities,
psychiatric hospitals, community and specialty hospitals, nursing facilities, and
prisons;
(2) Outpatient settings, such as clinics, medical offices, and therapist
offices;
(3) Home and community settings, such as homes, group homes,
assisted living facilities, schools, early intervention centers, daycare centers,
industrial and business facilities, hospices, sheltered workshops, wellness and
fitness centers, and community mental health facilities;
(4) Research facilities;
(5) Educational institutions; and
(6) Telehealth, telemedicine, or provider-based telemedicine, as
authorized by § 63-1-155.
63-33-1703. Applicant requirements – Examinations.
- 183 - 012037

In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as an
occupational therapist or as an occupational therapy assistant must:
(1) Have successfully completed the academic requirements of an
educational program accredited by ACOTE or its predecessor organization. The
accredited program must be a program for occupational therapists or a program
for occupational therapy assistants, depending upon the category of licensure for
which the applicant is applying;
(2) Have successfully completed the period of supervised fieldwork
experience required by ACOTE; and
(3) Have made an acceptable score on a written or computerized
examination designed to test the applicant's knowledge of the basic and clinical
services related to occupational therapy, occupational therapy techniques and
methods, and other subjects that may help to determine an applicant's fitness to
practice. The commissioner shall approve an examination for occupational
therapists and an examination for occupational therapy assistants and establish
standards for acceptable performance on each examination. The commissioner
may use the entry level national examinations prepared and administered by
NBCOT as the examinations used to test applicants for licensure as occupational
therapists or occupational therapy assistants and may use the standards of
NBCOT in determining an acceptable score on each examination.
63-33-1704. Limited permit.
(a) A limited permit may be issued by the commissioner to an applicant who has
applied for a license under this part and part 1 of this chapter, has successfully
completed the educational and field experience requirements of § 63-33-1703(1) and
(2), and is scheduled to take the examination required by § 63-33-1703(3).
(b) An applicant who has received a limited permit shall take the examination
within ninety (90) days of the date the applicant received the limited permit. If the
- 184 - 012037

applicant does not take the examination within that ninety-day period, then the limited
permit expires at the end of the ninety-day period.
(c) If an applicant fails the examination, then the applicant's limited permit
expires upon the division's receipt of notice that the applicant failed the examination.
(d) If an applicant passes the examination, then the applicant's limited permit
remains effective until the commissioner grants or denies a license to the applicant.
(e) An applicant may obtain a limited permit only once.
(f) A limited permit allows an applicant to engage in occupational therapy
practice under the supervision of a licensed occupational therapist.
(g) The commissioner shall adopt rules in accordance with the Uniform
Administrative Procedures Act, compiled in title 4, chapter 5, governing the supervision
of persons to whom a limited permit has been issued. The rules must address, at a
minimum, initial and periodic inspections, written evaluations, written treatment plans,
patient notes, and periodic evaluation of performance.
63-33-1705. Supervision of licensed occupation therapy assistants required.
(a) A licensed occupational therapy assistant shall practice under the
supervision of an occupational therapist who is licensed in this state.
(b) The supervising occupational therapist is responsible for all services
provided by the occupational therapy assistant, including, but not limited to, the
formulation and implementation of a plan of occupational therapy services for each
client, and has a continuing responsibility to follow the progress of each client and to
ensure the effective and appropriate supervision of the occupational therapy assistant
according to the needs of the client.
(c) The supervising occupational therapist shall assign to the occupational
therapy assistant only those duties and responsibilities that the occupational therapy
assistant is qualified to perform.
- 185 - 012037

(d) The commissioner shall adopt rules in accordance with the Uniform
Administrative Procedures Act, compiled in title 4, chapter 5, governing the supervision
of occupational therapy assistants by occupational therapists. Those rules may address
the following:
(1) The manner in which the supervising occupational therapist oversees
the work of the occupational therapy assistant;
(2) The ratio of occupational therapists to occupational therapy assistants
required under different conditions and in different practice settings; and
(3) The documentation of supervision contacts between the supervising
occupational therapist and the occupational therapy assistant.
(e) The rules adopted by the commissioner must recognize that the frequency,
methods, and content of supervision of occupational therapy assistants by occupational
therapists may vary by practice setting and are dependent upon the following factors,
among others:
(1) Complexity of the client's needs;
(2) Number and diversity of clients;
(3) Skills of the occupational therapy assistant and the supervising
occupational therapist;
(4) Type of practice setting; and
(5) Requirements of the practice setting.
63-33-1706. Authorized duties of unlicensed persons.
(a) A licensed physician, occupational therapist, or licensed occupational
therapy assistant may delegate to an unlicensed person specific routine tasks
associated with nontreatment aspects of occupational therapy practice that are not
evaluative, assessive, or task selective in nature and do not require making
recommendations, making decisions, or making assessment or treatment entries in
official patient records, if the following conditions are met:
- 186 - 012037

(1) The physician, occupational therapist, or occupational therapy
assistant accepts professional responsibility for the performance of that duty by
the person to whom it is delegated. In the case of duties delegated by an
occupational therapy assistant, the occupational therapy assistant, the physician,
and the occupational therapist who supervises the occupational therapy assistant
are responsible;
(2) The unlicensed person does not perform duties that require licensure
under this part and part 1 of this chapter; and
(3) The physician, occupational therapist, or occupational therapy
assistant ensures that the unlicensed person has been appropriately trained for
the performance of the tasks.
(b) Tasks that may be delegated include:
(1) Transporting of patients;
(2) Preparing or setting up a work area or equipment;
(3) Routine department maintenance or housekeeping activities;
(4) Taking care of a patient's personal needs during treatments; and
(5) Clerical, secretarial, or administrative duties.
63-33-1707. Exempted persons – Dry needling by licensed occupational
therapists not deemed acupuncture.
(a) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent or restrict the practice,
services, or activities of:
(1) A person licensed under this title who is authorized to provide
therapeutic services as listed under this part;
(2) A person employed as an occupational therapist or occupational
therapy assistant by an agency of the United States government while providing
occupational therapy services in that capacity;
- 187 - 012037

(3) A person pursuing a course of study leading to a degree or certificate
in occupational therapy in an educational program accredited or granted
developing program status by ACOTE, if:
(A) The activities and services constitute a part of a supervised
course of study; and
(B) The person is designated by a title that clearly indicates the
person's status as a student;
(4) A person fulfilling the supervised fieldwork experience requirements
of § 63-33-1703(2), if the activities and services constitute a part of the
experience necessary to meet the requirements of § 63-33-1703(2);
(5) An occupational therapist or occupational therapy assistant who is
licensed or certified to practice in another state that has licensure or certification
requirements at least as stringent as the requirements of this part while in this
state for the purpose of providing educational, consulting, or training services for
no more than fourteen (14) days in a calendar year; and
(6) A person who is certified by the National Council for Therapeutic
Recreation Certification as a certified therapeutic recreation specialist, while
engaged in practicing the profession of recreation therapy.
(b) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent certified orthotists from
designing, fabricating, and fitting orthotic devices.
(c) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent a person employed by a
physician from performing activities related to casting and splinting or teaching exercises
related to specific treatment by the employing physician.
(d) The practice of dry needling of the upper limb by an occupational therapist
licensed under this part and part 1 of this chapter does not constitute the practice of
acupuncture under part 4 of this chapter.
63-33-1708. Disciplinary grounds.
- 188 - 012037

In addition to the disciplinary grounds listed in § 63-33-106(b), the commissioner
may also exercise the powers enumerated in § 63-33-106(a) for the following:
(1) Making or signing in one's professional capacity a certificate that is
known to be false at the time one makes or signs the certificate;
(2) Soliciting by agents or persons generally known as "cappers" or
"steerers" of professional patronage or profiting by the acts of those representing
themselves to be agents of the licensee;
(3) Dividing fees or agreeing to split or divide fees received for
professional services with a person for bringing or referring a patient;
(4) Conducting practice so as to permit, directly or indirectly, an
unlicensed person to perform services or work that, under this part, can be done
legally only by persons licensed to practice;
(5) Professionally connecting or associating with a person, firm, or
corporation, in any manner, in an effort to avoid and circumvent this part or
lending one's name to another for illegal practice;
(6) Paying or accepting commissions, in any form or manner, on fees for
professional services, references, consultations, pathological reports,
prescriptions, or other services or articles supplied to patients;
(7) Giving of testimonials, directly or indirectly, concerning the supposed
virtue of secret therapeutic agents or proprietary preparations, such as remedies,
or other articles or materials that are offered to the public, claiming radical cure or
prevention of diseases by their use; and
(8) Using or participating in the use of any form of public communication
containing a false, fraudulent, misleading, or deceptive statement or claim on
behalf of the licensee or the licensee's partner, associate, or any other person
affiliated with the licensee or the licensee's facility.
63-33-1709. Violations – Use of titles – Unlicensed practice.
- 189 - 012037

(a) It is unlawful for a person to violate this part.
(b) It is unlawful for a person who is not licensed under this part as an
occupational therapist or an occupational therapy assistant or whose license has been
suspended or revoked to use, in connection with the person's name or place of
business, the words "occupational therapist," "occupational therapist registered,"
"licensed occupational therapist," "occupational therapy assistant," "certified
occupational therapy assistant" or "licensed occupational therapy assistant," the letters
"OT," "OTA," "OTR," "OT/L," "OTA/L," "COTA," or any other words, letters,
abbreviations, or insignia indicating or implying that the person is an occupational
therapist or an occupational therapy assistant or who in any way, orally, in writing, in
print or by sign, directly or by implication, claims to be an occupational therapist or an
occupational therapy assistant.
(c) A violation of this part constitutes unlicensed practice as set forth in § 63-33-
107.
63-33-1710. Requirements of applicants educated outside the United States.
Applicants for licensure who have completed educational programs outside the
United States shall furnish proof of good moral character and of completion of an
educational program and supervised fieldwork substantially similar to those contained in
§ 63-33-1703(1) and (2) and satisfy the examination requirements of § 63-33-1703(3).
63-33-1711. Requirements of an occupational therapist for dry needling.
In addition to the powers and duties granted to or imposed by this chapter, the
commissioner has the authority to establish minimum competency requirements that an
occupational therapist must demonstrate in order to practice dry needling of the upper
limb.
SECTION 84. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-1801. Part definitions.
- 190 - 012037

As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
(1) "Advertise" includes the issuing or causing to be distributed a card,
sign, or device to a person, or the causing, permitting, or allowing a sign or
marking on or in a building or structure, or in a newspaper or magazine, in a
directory, or on radio or television or by advertising by any other means designed
to secure public attention;
(2) "Appraisal activities":
(A) Means selecting, administering, scoring, and interpreting
instruments designed to assess an individual's aptitudes, achievements,
or interests, which are used to understand, measure, or facilitate the
individual's normal human growth and development, but does not include
the use of projective techniques in the assessment of personality, nor the
use of psychological or clinical tests designed to identify or classify
abnormal or pathological human behavior, nor the use of individually
administered intelligence tests; and
(B) Includes with regard to licensed professional counselors,
consistent with each counselor's formal education and training,
administering and utilizing appropriate assessment instruments that
measure or diagnose problems or dysfunctions within the context of
human growth and development as part of the counseling process or in
the development of a treatment plan;
(3) "Approved supervisor" means a licensed marital and family therapist,
psychologist, or psychiatrist who is either an American Association for Marriage
and Family Therapy-approved supervisor or a commissioner-approved marriage
and family supervisor;
(4) "Commissioner-approved marriage and family supervisor" means a
person who gives to the commissioner evidence of:
- 191 - 012037

(A) Five (5) years of full-time experience in marriage and family
therapy practice and supervision;
(B) Thirty-six (36) hours of supervision specifically in the skill of
providing marriage and family therapy supervision; and
(C) A recommendation for commissioner-approved supervisor
status from a supervisor who provided supervision for the supervision
referred to in subdivision (a)(4)(B);
(5) "Counseling" means assisting an individual, through the counseling
relationship, in a manner intended to facilitate normal human growth and
development, using a combination of mental health and human development
principles, methods, and techniques, to achieve mental, emotional, physical,
social, moral, educational, spiritual, or career development and adjustment
throughout the life span;
(6) "Licensed marital and family therapist" means a person to whom a
license has been issued pursuant to this part, which license is in force and not
suspended or revoked as of the particular time in question;
(7) "Licensed professional counselor" means a person licensed under
this part who is professionally trained in counseling and guidance services
designed to facilitate normal human growth and development through individual,
family, or group counseling, educational procedures, assessment, consultation,
and research and who assists individuals by the practice of counseling with their
personal, social, career, or educational development as they pass through life
stages;
(8) "Marital and family therapy" means the diagnosis and treatment of
cognitive, affective, and behavioral problems and dysfunctions within the context
of marital and family systems, and involves the professional application of
psychotherapeutic family systems theories and techniques in the delivery of
- 192 - 012037

services to individuals in the context of family systems theory and practice,
couples, and families;
(9) "Practice of counseling":
(A) Means rendering or offering to render to individuals, groups,
organizations, or the general public a service involving the application of
principles, techniques, methods, or procedures of the counseling
profession, including appraisal activities, counseling, consulting, and
referral activities; and
(B) Does not include permitting the treatment of a mental,
emotional, or adjustment disorder other than marital problems, parent-
child problems, child and adolescent antisocial behavior, adult antisocial
behavior, other specified family circumstances, other interpersonal
problems, phase of life problems, other life circumstance problems,
occupational problems, and uncomplicated bereavement, except as
provided in subdivision (10);
(10) "Practice of counseling as a mental health service provider":
(A) Means the application of mental health and human
development principles in order to:
(i) Facilitate human development and adjustment
throughout the life span;
(ii) Prevent, diagnose, and treat mental, emotional, or
behavioral disorders and associated disorders that interfere with
mental health;
(iii) Conduct assessments and diagnoses for the purpose
of establishing treatment goals and objectives within the
limitations prescribed in subdivision (2); and
- 193 - 012037

(iv) Plan, implement, and evaluate treatment plans using
counseling treatment interventions. As used in this subdivision
(10)(A)(iv), "counseling treatment interventions" means the
application of cognitive, affective, behavioral, and systemic
counseling strategies that include principles of development,
wellness, and pathology that reflect a pluralistic society; and
(B) Does not include the performance of an act that licensed
professional counselors designated as mental health service providers
are not educated and trained to perform or the designation of testing
reports as "psychological";
(11) "Practice of marital and family therapy" means the rendering of
professional marital and family therapy to individuals, couples, and family groups,
singly or in groups, whether such services are offered directly to the general
public or through organizations, either public or private, for a fee;
(12) "Recognized educational institution" means an educational
institution that is recognized by the commissioner and by a nationally or
regionally recognized educational or professional accrediting body;
(13) "Supervision" means the direct clinical review, for the purpose of
training or teaching, by an approved supervisor of a marriage and family
therapist's interaction with clients, where the purpose of supervision is to promote
the development of the practitioner's clinical skills; such supervision may include,
without being limited to, the review of case presentations, audiotapes,
videotapes, and direct observation; and
(14) "Use a title or description of" means to hold oneself out to the public
as having a particular status by means of stating such status on signs,
mailboxes, address plates, stationery, announcements, business cards, or other
instruments of professional identification.
- 194 - 012037

63-33-1802. Reciprocity for marital and family therapist applicants.
(a) The commissioner shall license without examination a marital and family
therapist applicant who is licensed to practice independently in another state if the
applicant's qualifications meet the licensure requirements under this part and part 1 of
this chapter.
(b) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses marital and family therapists.
63-33-1803. Required documentation from professional counselor applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
professional counselor must provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1)
(A) Has a conferred graduate degree in counseling or a closely
related field;
(B) Has obtained a total of sixty (60) graduate hours in counseling
or a closely related field; and
(C) Has completed a supervised field experience as either a
practicum or internship;
(2) Has had at least two (2) years of professional experience of a type
judged to be acceptable by the commissioner subsequent to being granted a
graduate degree and has not violated § 63-33-106 or § 63-33-1805;
(3) Has passed the examination offered by the National Board for
Certified Counselors (NBCC) or such other examination approved by the
commissioner;
(4) Has passed the jurisprudence exam in this state; and
(5) Has met additional criteria of the commissioner established by rule.
63-33-1804. Required documentation from marital and family therapist applicants.
- 195 - 012037

(a) In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
marital and family therapist must provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Has met standards set by the commissioner no less stringent than the
American Association for Marriage and Family Therapy's standards for a clinical
member so long as such standards specify a minimum of a master's level
degree; and
(2) Has passed such examination as may be required by the
commissioner.
(b) Applicants shall bear the fee for testing in addition to the review fee and
application fee.
63-33-1805. Disciplinary grounds.
In addition to the disciplinary grounds listed in § 63-33-106(b), the commissioner
may also exercise the powers enumerated in § 63-33-106(a) for the following:
(1) Using fraud or deception in taking an examination required by this
part; or
(2) Violating the rules adopted by the commissioner, except that a
violation of A.11.b of the 2014 American Counseling Association Code of Ethics,
or any similar or successor provision, is not grounds upon which the
commissioner shall exercise the commissioner's powers to discipline a license;
however, a violation of A.11.b is a ground for the commissioner to exercise these
powers in cases involving an individual seeking or undergoing counseling where
the individual was in imminent danger of harming themselves or others.
63-33-1806. Exempted persons.
(a) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not apply to a person if the person is
preparing for the practice of marital and family therapy under qualified supervision in a
training institution or facility or supervisory arrangement recognized and approved by the
- 196 - 012037

commissioner as long as the person is designated by such titles as "marital therapy
intern," "family therapy trainee," or others clearly indicating such training status.
(b) This part and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent:
(1) Qualified members of other professional groups as defined by the
commissioner by rule, including, but not limited to, licensed clinical social
workers, licensed psychologists, licensed psychological examiners, licensed
senior psychological examiners, certified psychological assistants, psychiatric
nurses, physicians, attorneys at law, or members of the clergy from doing or
advertising that they perform the work of a marital and family therapy nature
consistent with the accepted standards of their respective professions; and
(2) Alcohol and drug abuse counselors licensed under chapter 11, part 4
of this title or operating under qualified supervision while seeking such
certification from doing counseling consistent with the accepted standards of that
profession.
63-33-1807. Confidential relations and communications.
The confidential relations and communications between licensed marital and
family therapists, licensed professional counselors, or certified pastoral therapists and
clients are placed upon the same basis as those provided by law between attorney and
client. This part does not require such privileged communication to be disclosed.
However, this section and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent disclosures of confidential
communications in proceedings arising under title 37, chapter 1, part 4 concerning
mandatory child abuse reports.
63-33-1808. Prohibited conduct by unlicensed persons – Exemptions.
(a) Except as provided in § 63-33-1806, a person who is not licensed or certified
as a marital and family therapist under this part shall not:
(1) Advertise the performance of marital and family therapy or counseling
service by the person; or
- 197 - 012037

(2) Use a title or description, including, but not limited to, "licensed,"
"certified," "marriage," "marital," "therapist," "counselor," "advisor," or
"consultant," or any other name, style, or description denoting that the person is
a marital and family therapist or practices marital and family therapy.
(b) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section commits
a Class B misdemeanor.
(c) This part does not permit a person licensed or certified as a marital and
family therapist to engage in the practice of "licensed psychological examiner," "licensed
senior psychological examiner," "certified psychological assistant," "licensed
psychologist," or "licensed social worker," as defined in the laws of this state.
(d) This part, except subsection (a), does not apply to a person regulated by the
board of nursing.
(e) This part does not permit a person certified or licensed as a marital and
family therapist to perform psychological testing intended to measure or diagnose mental
illness. Consistent with each therapist's formal education and training, licensed marital
and family therapists may administer and utilize appropriate assessment instruments
that measure or diagnose cognitive, affective, and behavioral problems and dysfunctions
of individuals in the context of marital and family systems, couples, and families as part
of the therapy process or in the development of a treatment plan.
63-33-1809. Reciprocity for professional counselors.
(a)
(1) In accordance with § 63-33-104, the commissioner may issue a
license to a professional counselor applicant with a valid, unencumbered license
issued by another state, territory, or federal district of the United States at an
equivalent level of licensure under the following conditions:
(A) The applicant has a sixty-hour graduate degree in counseling
or a related field, meets the requirements of § 63-33-1803(2)-(5), and has
- 198 - 012037

actively practiced without supervision at the level of licensure for which
the applicant has applied for at least two (2) of the three (3) most recent
years; or
(B) The applicant has a conferred graduate degree consisting of a
minimum of fifty-two (52) hours in counseling or a related field from an
accredited program that were earned prior to 2016, has practiced as a
licensed professional counselor for a minimum of twenty-five (25) years,
and meets the requirements of § 63-33-1803(2)-(5).
(2) A professional counselor applicant at the highest level of licensure
must meet the requirements of § 63-33-1813, as well as the requirements of
either subdivision (a)(1)(A) or (a)(1)(B).
(b) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses, certifies, or registers professional counselors, if the board finds that such state
has substantially the same or higher licensure requirements than this state. The
agreement must provide that the board shall license a resident of another state who is
currently licensed, certified, or registered by that state, if the resident has met the same
or higher requirements as provided for in this part.
(c) If the commissioner has entered into a reciprocal agreement with another
state in accordance with § 63-33-104(b) on or before January 1, 2024, then the
commissioner must grant a license to a person who:
(1) Has a master's degree in counseling or education;
(2) Has a valid, unencumbered license in the state with which this state
has a reciprocal agreement;
(3) Has actively practiced for at least the preceding twenty-four (24)
months in the state with which this state has such reciprocal agreement; and
- 199 - 012037

(4) Has passed the examination offered by the National Board for
Certified Counselors (NBCC) or such other examination approved by the
commissioner.
63-33-1810. Unlawful use of titles – Exempt persons.
(a)
(1) Except as specifically provided elsewhere in this part, commencing
July 1, 2026, it is an offense for a person to engage in the following acts:
(A) Representing or advertising the person as, or using a title or
description such as, "licensed professional counselor" without being duly
licensed according to this part;
(B) Making use of a title, words, letters, or abbreviations, or any
combination thereof, that may reasonably be confused with licensure
provided by this part to denote a standard of professional or occupational
competence, without being duly licensed under this part; or
(C) Performing activities that may reasonably be construed to fall
within the defined scope of practice of persons licensed under this part
who are designated as mental health service providers as defined in § 63-
33-1813 without being duly licensed under this part.
(2) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section
commits a Class B misdemeanor.
(3) In addition to subdivisions (a)(1) and (2), the department of health
may institute appropriate proceedings, in law or equity, to enjoin a person from
engaging in an unlawful act enumerated in this section, such action or
proceeding to be brought in the circuit or chancery court of the county in which
the unlawful act occurs or in which the defendant resides.
(b) This part does not permit a person licensed or certified as a professional
counselor or designated as a mental health service provider under this part and part 1 of
- 200 - 012037

this chapter to engage in the practice of licensed psychological examiner, licensed
senior psychological examiner, certified psychological assistant, licensed psychologist,
licensed social worker, psychiatric nurse, law, or medicine.
(c) This part does not apply to a person if the person is preparing for the practice
of professional counseling or the practice permitted to a person designated as a mental
health service provider pursuant to this chapter under qualified supervision.
(d) This part does not:
(1) Limit the ministry, activities, or services of a rabbi, priest, minister of
the gospel, or others authorized by a regularly organized and functioning
religious body in performing the ordinary duties or functions of the clergy;
(2) Apply to or limit the activities or services of Christian Science
practitioners; or
(3) Limit a rabbi, priest, or minister who offers counseling services, even
if fees are charged, as long as they do not hold themselves out as certified or
licensed professional counselors.
63-33-1811. Exempted professionals.
(a) Except § 63-33-1810, this part does not apply to:
(1) Persons regulated by the board of nursing;
(2) Persons regulated by the state board of education; and
(3) Professional counselors employed in community or human services
agencies and working directly under the supervision of a licensed professional
counselor.
(b) This part does not prevent members of other professional groups, including,
without limitation, licensed social workers, psychologists, psychiatrists, and other
physicians, attorneys, or members of the clergy, from performing or advertising their
respective professions as long as such persons do not violate § 63-33-1810.
63-33-1812. Application of chapter 11 of this title.
- 201 - 012037

Notwithstanding this part to the contrary, a person licensed pursuant to this part
and chapter 11 of this title is subject to the limitations of chapter 11 of this title.
63-33-1813. Requirements of mental health service providers.
A professional counselor licensed under this part and designated as a mental
health service provider must have:
(1) Completed coursework specifically related to the diagnosis,
treatment, appraisal, and assessment of mental disorders; and
(2) Completed two (2) years of postgraduate supervised experience
required for licensure in a clinical setting that provides substantial opportunities to
diagnose, treat, appraise, and assess mental disorders.
63-33-1814. Temporary licenses.
(a)
(1) A temporary license may be issued by the commissioner for a
licensed professional counselor designated as a mental health service provider
applicant who has completed the academic coursework and training required for
the license sought and who has successfully passed the examination required by
the commissioner.
(2) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes an
applicant to perform the functions constituting the practice of counseling as a
mental health service provider, for which the applicant is seeking licensure under
qualified supervision.
(3) In order to receive a temporary license, an applicant must submit to
the division a completed application for a temporary license with the applicant's
completed application for the desired license and all appropriate fees.
(4) If an applicant is granted a temporary license, then the license must
remain valid for up to four (4) years and is eligible for extension at the discretion
of the commissioner.
- 202 - 012037

(5) The applicant shall notify the division and present supporting
documentation demonstrating the satisfactory completion of the required
postgraduate supervised experience in a clinical setting. The commissioner shall
then grant or deny the license application based on satisfactory completion of all
requirements for licensure.
(b)
(1) A temporary license may be issued by the commissioner to a marital
and family therapist applicant who has completed the academic coursework and
training required for the license sought. In order to retain the temporary license,
the applicant must take the written examination required by the commissioner the
first time it is scheduled following issuance of the temporary license. The
applicant shall successfully pass the exam within two (2) years following
issuance of the temporary license.
(2) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes the
applicant to engage in the practice of marital and family therapy under the
supervision of an approved supervisor.
(3) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant must submit to
the division the following:
(A) A completed application for a temporary license;
(B) Satisfactory evidence of an agreement with an approved
supervisor under whose supervision the applicant intends to practice; and
(C) All appropriate fees.
(4) A temporary license is nonrenewable and valid for a period of no
more than three (3) years. Within such three-year period, the applicant shall
submit to the division an application for the regular license and present
supporting documentation demonstrating the satisfactory completion of the
required amount of post-master's degree supervised experience in a clinical
- 203 - 012037

setting under an approved supervisor. The commissioner shall then grant or
deny the application for the regular license, based on satisfactory completion of
all requirements for licensure, including the oral examination. If the
commissioner approves or denies the application for the regular license or
revokes the temporary license for any reason, then the temporary license ceases
to be valid and must be returned to the division.
(5) The holder of a temporary license as a marital and family therapist
shall not represent the temporary licensee to be a licensed marital and family
therapist. The holder of the temporary license shall only represent the temporary
licensee to be a "marital therapy intern," a "family therapy trainee," or such other
title designation that clearly reflects trainee status and temporary licensure.
SECTION 85. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-1901. Part definitions.
As used in this part:
(1) "Advertise" includes:
(A) Business solicitations, with or without limiting qualifications, in
a card, sign, or device issued to a person, in a sign or marking in or on a
building or in a newspaper, magazine, directory, or other printed matter;
and
(B) Business solicitations communicated by individual, radio,
video or television broadcasting, or other means designed to secure
public attention;
(2) "Certified clinical pastoral therapist" means a person who has met the
qualifications for certified clinical pastoral therapist and holds a current,
unsuspended or unrevoked certificate that has been lawfully issued by the
commissioner;
- 204 - 012037

(3) "Clinical pastoral education" means a program of training, typically
occurring in general medical, psychiatric, or penal institutions, that is designed to
acquaint students of theology and practicing clergy with the clinical method of
learning, increase skills in the arts of pastoral care, and facilitate integration of a
professional pastoral identity;
(4) "Clinical pastoral therapy" means the diagnosis and treatment, from a
clinical pastoral perspective, of the psychodynamics, interpersonal dynamics,
and spiritual dynamics of persons experiencing emotional behavioral or relational
distress or dysfunction, and involves the integration and professional application
of resources and techniques from the religious community's traditions of pastoral
care and counsel along with recognized principles, methods, and procedures of
the contemporary psychotherapy community in the delivery of counseling and
psychotherapeutic services to individuals, couples, families, and groups;
(5) "Licensed clinical pastoral therapist" means a person who has met
the qualifications for a licensed clinical pastoral therapist and who holds a
current, unsuspended or unrevoked license that has been issued lawfully by the
commissioner;
(6) "Practice of clinical pastoral therapy" means the rendering of
professional clinical pastoral therapy to individuals, couples, families, or groups,
either offered directly to the general public by an individual operating
independently of an institution, organization, or agency, through mental health
clinics or agencies, whether public or private, or through hospitals, whether public
or private, for a fee, excluding volunteer hours;
(7) "Recognized educational institution" means an educational institution
that is accredited by a nationally or regionally recognized educational accrediting
body;
(8) "Supervision":
- 205 - 012037

(A) Means the direct clinical review, for the purpose of training or
teaching, by a commissioner-approved supervisor, of a clinical pastoral
therapist's interaction with clients and promoting the development of the
practitioner's clinical skills; and
(B) Includes the review of case presentations, audiotapes,
videotapes, and direct observation; and
(9) "Use the title" means to hold oneself out to the public as having a
particular status by means of stating such status on signs, mailboxes, address
plates, stationery, announcements, business cards, or other instruments of
professional identification.
63-33-1902. Prohibited conduct by unlicensed persons – Exemptions.
(a) Except as specifically provided in § 63-33-1904, a person who is not licensed
as a clinical pastoral therapist under this part shall not:
(1) Advertise that the performance of clinical pastoral therapy services is
by a licensed clinical pastoral therapist; or
(2) Use the title "licensed clinical pastoral therapist" to denote that the
person is a licensed clinical pastoral therapist.
(b) A person who engages in an unlawful act enumerated in this section commits
a Class B misdemeanor.
(c) This section does not permit a person certified as a clinical pastoral therapist
to engage in the practice of licensed psychological examiner, licensed senior
psychological examiner, certified psychological assistant, licensed psychologist, or
licensed social worker, as defined in the laws of this state.
(d) This section does not apply to a person regulated by the board of nursing.
(e) This section does not permit a certified clinical pastoral therapist to prescribe
medications or to interpret psychological tests intended to measure or diagnose mental
illness.
- 206 - 012037

(f) Certified clinical pastoral therapists shall establish and maintain effective
working relationships with an interdisciplinary network of professionals, including at least
one (1) psychologically oriented physician, usually a psychiatrist, with an unlimited
license to practice the healing arts in this state, in order to make provision for referral for
the diagnosis and treatment of medical or mental conditions falling outside the scope of
clinical pastoral therapy.
63-33-1903. Documentation required from applicants.
In addition to the requirements of § 63-33-103, an applicant for licensure as a
clinical pastoral therapist shall provide documentation in the form required by the
commissioner that the applicant:
(1) Has met the educational standards set by the commissioner, which
must include:
(A) The completion of a course of studies consisting of a
minimum of sixty (60) graduate semester hours in a curriculum approved
by the commissioner, of which a minimum of nine (9) graduate semester
hours must relate specifically to the diagnosis and treatment of mental
disorders, and the awarding of a master's or doctoral degree from a
recognized educational institution; and
(B) The completion of a supervised clinical experience within the
academic degree program as either a practicum or internship that
includes experience in the assessment, diagnosis, and treatment of the
psychodynamics, interpersonal dynamics, and spiritual dynamics of
persons experiencing emotional, behavioral, relational, or spiritual
distress or dysfunction. The experience required under this subdivision
(1)(B) must be conducted under the supervision of a commissioner-
approved supervisor;
- 207 - 012037

(2) Has provided a minimum of one thousand four hundred (1,400) hours
of pastoral therapy with individuals, couples, families, or groups while receiving a
minimum of two hundred seventy (270) hours of supervision of such therapy
under commissioner-approved supervision; and
(3) Has passed examinations as approved by the commissioner.
63-33-1904. Religious, training, and professions exemptions.
(a) This part and part 18 of this chapter do not:
(1) Limit the ministry, activities, or services of a rabbi, priest, minister of
the gospel, or others authorized by a regularly organized and functioning
religious body in performing the ordinary duties or functions of the clergy;
(2) Apply to or limit the activities or services of Christian Science
practitioners; and
(3) Limit a rabbi, priest, or minister who offers counseling services, even
if fees are charged, as long as they do not hold themselves out as licensed
pastoral therapists or licensed pastoral counselors and do not purport to provide
the integration and professional application of resources and techniques from the
religious community's traditions of pastoral care and counsel along with
recognized principles, methods, and procedures of clinical psychotherapy.
(b) This part does not apply to a person if the person is preparing for the practice
of clinical pastoral therapy under qualified supervision in a training institution or facility or
supervisory arrangement recognized and approved by the commissioner as long as the
person is designated by such title as "pastoral therapy intern," "pastoral therapy trainee,"
or others clearly indicating such training status.
(c) This part does not prevent:
(1) Qualified members of other professional groups as defined by the
commissioner by rule, including, but not limited to, licensed clinical social
workers, licensed psychologists, licensed psychological examiners, licensed
- 208 - 012037

senior psychological examiners, certified psychological assistants, psychiatric
nurses, physicians, or attorneys at law, from performing or advertising that they
provide or offer counseling services consistent with the accepted standards of
their respective professions; and
(2) Alcohol and drug abuse counselors licensed under chapter 11, part 4
of this title or operating under qualified supervision while seeking such licensure
from doing counseling consistent with the accepted standards of such profession.
63-33-1905. Reciprocity – License by endorsement.
(a) The board may enter into a reciprocal agreement with any other state that
licenses, certifies, or registers clinical pastoral therapists, if the board finds that such
state has substantially the same or higher licensure requirements than this state. The
agreement must provide that the board may license without examination a resident of
another state who is currently licensed, certified, or registered by the state, if that
resident has met the same or higher requirements as provided in this part.
(b) The commissioner may license by endorsement a clinical pastoral therapist
applicant who is a fellow or diplomate of the American Association of Pastoral
Counselors if that person otherwise meets the requirements of this chapter.
(c) The commissioner may also license by endorsement a clinical pastoral
therapist applicant who is:
(1) Certified as a clinical member of the American Association of Pastoral
Counselors;
(2) Can document five (5) years of full-time practice in pastoral therapy
subsequent to AAPC certification; and
(3) Otherwise meets the requirements of this part.
63-33-1906. License for persons certified on or before June 3, 2003.
A person who was certified as a certified clinical pastoral therapist on or before
June 3, 2003, must be issued a license as a licensed clinical pastoral therapist when the
- 209 - 012037

person's certification is renewed or upon request of the person before the expiration of
the person's current certification.
63-33-1907. Temporary license.
(a) The commissioner may issue a temporary license to a clinical pastoral
therapist applicant who has completed the academic coursework and supervised clinical
experience for the license sought. In order to retain the temporary license, the applicant
must take the written examination required by the commissioner the first time it is
scheduled following issuance of the temporary license unless granted an extension by
the commissioner after submitting a written request to the division and making a showing
of good cause as determined by the commissioner. The applicant shall successfully
pass the exam within two (2) years following issuance of the temporary license unless
the applicant receives a good cause extension from the commissioner. An applicant
must only receive one (1) good cause extension from the commissioner.
(b) A temporary license obtained pursuant to this section authorizes the
applicant to engage in the practice of clinical pastoral therapy under the supervision of a
commissioner-approved supervisor.
(c) In order to receive a temporary license, the applicant must submit to the
division the following:
(1) A completed application for a temporary license;
(2) Satisfactory evidence of an agreement with a commissioner-approved
supervisor; and
(3) All required fees.
(d) A temporary license is nonrenewable and valid for a period of not more than
three (3) years. A temporary license may be extended beyond the three-year period at
the discretion of the commissioner if an applicant shows good cause for an extension as
determined by the commissioner. Only one (1) extension may be granted by the
commissioner for an applicant to extend the length of the applicant's temporary license.
- 210 - 012037

Within the period of temporary licensure, the applicant shall submit to the division an
application for the regular license and present supporting documentation demonstrating
the satisfactory completion of the required supervised clinical experience. The
commissioner shall then grant or deny the application for the regular license, based on
satisfactory completion of all requirements for licensure. If the commissioner approves
or denies the application for the regular license or revokes the temporary license for any
reason, then the temporary license ceases to be valid and must be returned to the
division.
(e) The holder of a temporary license as a clinical pastoral therapist shall not
represent the holder to be a licensed clinical pastoral therapist. The holder of a
temporary license as a clinical pastoral therapist shall only represent the holder to be a
"pastoral therapy intern," a "pastoral therapy trainee," or such other title designation that
clearly reflects trainee status and temporary licensure.
63-33-1908. Confidential relations and communications.
The confidential relations and communications between certified clinical pastoral
therapists and clients are placed upon the same basis as those provided by law between
attorney and client. This part does not require such privileged communication to be
disclosed. However, this section and part 1 of this chapter do not prevent disclosures of
confidential communications in proceedings arising under title 37, chapter 1, part 4,
concerning mandatory child abuse reports.
SECTION 86. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 63, Chapter 33, is amended by adding
the following as a new part:
63-33-2001. Part definitions.
As used in this part, "counseling or therapy services" means assisting an
individual, who is seeking or engaged in the counseling relationship in a private practice
setting, in a manner intended to facilitate normal human growth and development, using
a combination of mental health and human development principles, methods, and
- 211 - 012037

techniques, to achieve mental, emotional, physical, social, moral, educational, spiritual,
or career development and adjustment throughout the individual's life span.
63-33-2002. Client with goals, outcomes, or behaviors in conflict with sincerely
held principles of counselor or therapist – Refusal to provide counseling or therapy
services.
(a) A counselor or therapist providing counseling or therapy services is not
required to counsel or serve a client as to goals, outcomes, or behaviors that conflict
with the sincerely held principles of the counselor or therapist if the counselor or
therapist coordinates a referral of the client to another counselor or therapist who will
provide the counseling or therapy.
(b) The refusal to provide counseling or therapy services as described in
subsection (a) is not a basis for:
(1) A civil cause of action; or
(2) Criminal prosecution.
(c) Subsections (a) and (b) do not apply to a counselor or therapist when the
individual seeking or undergoing counseling is in imminent danger of harming
themselves or others.

SECTION 93. Tennessee Code Annotated, Title 68, Chapter 1, Part 1, is amended by
adding the following as a new section:
68-1-150. Rules.
(a) When legislation is enacted by the general assembly that requires a board
administratively attached to the department to promulgate rules in a prescribed period of
time, the board retains the exclusive authority to promulgate the rules until sixty (60)
days before the effective date of the legislation.
(b) If the board has not promulgated emergency rules and scheduled the
rulemaking hearing on permanent rules at least sixty (60) days before the effective date
- 214 - 012037

of the legislation, the commissioner becomes the exclusive authority to promulgate the
rules as described in subsection (a). Upon the receipt of such authority, the
commissioner shall, in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5:
(1) Promulgate emergency rules, in accordance with § 4-5-208, within
the time required by the legislation; and
(2) Promulgate permanent rules within one hundred eighty (180) days of
the effective date of the emergency rules.
(c) Upon the completion of the requirements of subsection (b), the exclusive
authority to promulgate rules reverts to the board. The board may, at that time, amend
the permanent rules in accordance with the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act,
compiled in title 4, chapter 5.
(d) The rules promulgated by the commissioner in accordance with subsection
(b) remain in full force and effect, the same as if promulgated by the board, unless and
until the rules are amended by the board.
SECTION 94. Tennessee Code Annotated, Section 68-1-2408, is amended by deleting
the section and substituting the following:
(a) Entities receiving grants shall report to the health care and services facility as
often as the department determines to be beneficial to program oversight.
(b) The health care and services facility shall report to the department as often
as the department determines to be beneficial to program oversight, but at least
annually.
(c) The department shall publish annually a summary of program participation
and outcome measures.

SECTION 103. Tennessee Code Annotated, Section 68-55-102(b), is amended by
deleting the subsection and substituting:
(b) The members are appointed to serve three-year or four-year terms. The
successor appointee for the half of the members with a service expiration closest in time
after July 1, 2026, shall serve three-year terms, while the other half of the members shall
serve four-year terms. Appointment of successors must match the three-year or four-
year term of the member they are appointed to succeed.
SECTION 104. The following rules are repealed on July 1, 2026:
(1) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0880-11;
(2) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0480-01;
(3) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0540-01, 0540-02, and 0540-03; and
(4) Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1200-10-02.
SECTION 105.
(a) The headings in this act are for reference purposes only and do not
constitute a part of the law enacted by this act. However, the Tennessee Code
Commission is requested to include the headings in any compilation or publication
containing this act.
(b) The use of "[former]" and "[repealed]" in this act are for notation purposes
only and do not constitute a part of the law enacted by this act. However, the
- 217 - 012037

Tennessee Code Commission is requested to include such notations in any compilation
or publication containing this act.
(c) The Tennessee Code Commission is requested to reserve parts 10 and 11 in
title 63, chapter 33.
SECTION 106. This act takes effect on July 1, 2026, the public welfare requiring it.
